5 min
The Rejection of Authentic Narration in Western Approaches
Author gives first reason: rejection of narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Western thinkers' disregard for authentic narration makes convergence with Islamic thought impossible.

Core Idea
Western thinkers discarded the very foundation of Islamic knowledge: reliable narration.

The author begins by stating that there is no hope of convergence between Muslim and Western thinkers regarding revelation. He immediately points to a fundamental difference: Western thinkers have completely abandoned the institution of narration (riwaya) and its scientific value. This lesson explores that first reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the author's absolute statement 'ليس ثمة مطمع' (there is no hope).
This sets the tone.
2
Identify the two permissions
The author says Western thinkers have allowed themselves two things: ignoring authentic mutawatir narration and inventing unsupported interpretations. Identify both.
These two permissions are symmetrical.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does discarding narration prevent convergence? Because Islamic methodology relies on authenticated reports. Without accepting their value, common ground is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس ثمة مطمع في أن يلتقي هؤلاء ومفكرو الإسلام على صراط واحد من الفهم في الأمر ، إذ إن هؤلاء قد أسقطوا من اعتبارهم أمر الـروايــة والخبر وقيمتها العلمية سلباً وإيجاباً ، أي إنهم استجازوا لأنفسهم تجاهل الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة كما استجازوا في نفس الوقت اختراع تفسير لا يدعمه أي خبر أو رواية صحيحة . كما أنهم لم يلتزموا إطلاقاً بمنهج الاستقراء وما يثبته قانون الالتزام وقياس الأولى ، ولذلك جاز لهم أن يصوروا من محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام منذ اللحظة التي أوحي فيها إليه ، شخصية تتناقض كلياً مع شخصيته السابقة بل مع وقائع حياته المستمرة أيضاً ، وجاز لهم أن يجعلوا منه عليه الصلاة والسلام أعظم كذاب
And there is no hope that these [Western thinkers] and Muslim thinkers will meet on a single path of understanding in the matter, because these [Westerners] have discarded from consideration the matter of narration and report and its scientific value, both positively and negatively. That is, they have permitted themselves to ignore the authentic mutawatir narration, while at the same time they permitted themselves to invent an interpretation that is not supported by any report or authentic narration. Moreover, they have not adhered at all to the methodology of induction and what the law of commitment and the analogy of the higher establish. Therefore, they have allowed themselves to depict Muhammad, peace be upon him, from the moment revelation came to him, as a personality that totally contradicts his previous personality, and even contradicts the ongoing facts of his life, and they have allowed themselves to make him, peace be upon him, the greatest liar.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage gives the reasons why Islamic and Western approaches to revelation can never converge. The author states that Western thinkers have completely disregarded the institution of narration (riwaya) and the scientific value of reports, both in affirming and denying. They have allowed themselves to ignore authentic mutawatir narrations and, simultaneously, to invent interpretations that have no basis in any authentic report or narration. Furthermore, they have not adhered to the methodology of induction (istiqra') and what is established by the law of commitment (qanun al-iltizam) and analogy of the higher (qiyas al-awla). Consequently, they have been able to portray the Prophet from the moment of revelation as a person totally contradicting his earlier character and even contradicting the ongoing facts of his life, even going so far as to call him the greatest liar. The passage underscores that the methodological differences are so fundamental that no common understanding is possible.

Key Terms
الرواية
التواتر
الخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author claims all Western scholars are insincere or malicious.
Correction: The author is pointing to a methodological choice that necessarily leads to certain outcomes, not necessarily to personal bad faith.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two things have Western thinkers allowed themselves regarding narration?
A) Ignoring weak narrations and inventing weak interpretations
B) Ignoring authentic mutawatir narrations and inventing unsupported interpretations
C) Rejecting all narrations and using only reason
D) Accepting unreliable narrations and rejecting authentic ones

Key Takeaway
The fundamental obstacle to convergence is the rejection of narration as a valid source of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Western thinkers 'permitted themselves to ignore the authentic mutawatir narration' and 'invent an interpretation not supported by any authentic report.' Have you ever caught yourself doing the same—ignoring a clear proof in the Quran or sunnah because it didn't fit your preferred view? What would you have to give up to submit fully to transmitted truth?
?
The author says there is no hope for convergence if narration is discarded. Where in your own heart do you rely more on your own reasoning and feelings than on what has been reliably reported from the Prophet ﷺ? Are you willing to change that today by actively seeking out and accepting authentic narrations even when they are difficult?
?
Imagine you are faced with an opinion from a respected modern thinker that contradicts a authentic narration you know. Which one will you trust, and what does your trust reveal about your true epistemological foundation? Commit to one concrete action this week that strengthens your reliance on prophetic transmission.

Methodological Divide: Induction and Analogy
Author gives second reason: rejection of induction and its consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rejection of induction, the law of commitment, and analogy of the higher leads to distortions of the Prophet's character.

Core Idea
Without proper methodology, even the Prophet's life can be misrepresented.

The author continues his diagnosis of why Islamic and Western approaches cannot converge. He adds a second reason: Western thinkers have abandoned the methodology of induction (istiqra') and the rational principles that follow from it, such as the law of commitment and the analogy of the higher. This lesson examines that second reason and its shocking consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'كما أنهم لم يلتزموا' to the end. Note the logical connector 'ولذلك' (therefore) linking methodology to consequence.
2
Understand the three methodological tools
Identify induction (الاستقراء), law of commitment (قانون الالتزام), and analogy of the higher (قياس الأولى). The commentary will explain them briefly.
These are cognitive tools that prevent arbitrary interpretation.
3
Observe the consequence
The author says because they abandoned these tools, they could depict the Prophet as a contradictory figure and even call him the greatest liar. How does abandoning methodology lead to such conclusions?
This shows the stakes of methodological disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس ثمة مطمع في أن يلتقي هؤلاء ومفكرو الإسلام على صراط واحد من الفهم في الأمر ، إذ إن هؤلاء قد أسقطوا من اعتبارهم أمر الـروايــة والخبر وقيمتها العلمية سلباً وإيجاباً ، أي إنهم استجازوا لأنفسهم تجاهل الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة كما استجازوا في نفس الوقت اختراع تفسير لا يدعمه أي خبر أو رواية صحيحة . كما أنهم لم يلتزموا إطلاقاً بمنهج الاستقراء وما يثبته قانون الالتزام وقياس الأولى ، ولذلك جاز لهم أن يصوروا من محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام منذ اللحظة التي أوحي فيها إليه ، شخصية تتناقض كلياً مع شخصيته السابقة بل مع وقائع حياته المستمرة أيضاً ، وجاز لهم أن يجعلوا منه عليه الصلاة والسلام أعظم كذاب
And there is no hope that these [Western thinkers] and Muslim thinkers will meet on a single path of understanding in the matter, because these [Westerners] have discarded from consideration the matter of narration and report and its scientific value, both positively and negatively. That is, they have permitted themselves to ignore the authentic mutawatir narration, while at the same time they permitted themselves to invent an interpretation that is not supported by any report or authentic narration. Moreover, they have not adhered at all to the methodology of induction and what the law of commitment and the analogy of the higher establish. Therefore, they have allowed themselves to depict Muhammad, peace be upon him, from the moment revelation came to him, as a personality that totally contradicts his previous personality, and even contradicts the ongoing facts of his life, and they have allowed themselves to make him, peace be upon him, the greatest liar.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage gives the reasons why Islamic and Western approaches to revelation can never converge. The author states that Western thinkers have completely disregarded the institution of narration (riwaya) and the scientific value of reports, both in affirming and denying. They have allowed themselves to ignore authentic mutawatir narrations and, simultaneously, to invent interpretations that have no basis in any authentic report or narration. Furthermore, they have not adhered to the methodology of induction (istiqra') and what is established by the law of commitment (qanun al-iltizam) and analogy of the higher (qiyas al-awla). Consequently, they have been able to portray the Prophet from the moment of revelation as a person totally contradicting his earlier character and even contradicting the ongoing facts of his life, even going so far as to call him the greatest liar. The passage underscores that the methodological differences are so fundamental that no common understanding is possible.

Key Terms
الاستقراء
قانون الالتزام
قياس الأولى
محمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author say Western thinkers have not adhered to?
A) The methodology of deduction
B) The methodology of induction and the principles it establishes
C) The methodology of experimentation
D) The methodology of historical criticism

Key Takeaway
Abandoning sound methodology leads to the most extreme distortions, including misrepresenting the Prophet's character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you form an opinion about someone else’s character, do you gather enough evidence to avoid the kind of contradiction described in this lesson? What would change if you applied induction to your judgments?
?
The law of commitment forces you to accept the logical implications of your premises. If your premise is that the Prophet was truthful and consistent, what must you necessarily conclude about the claims that he was a liar? Are you willing to follow that implication fully?
?
You will encounter many distorted portrayals of the Prophet in media and academic works. How will you use the methodological tools from this lesson—especially induction and analogy of the higher—to critically evaluate those portrayals rather than passively accept them?

Revelation as Objective Reality
Buti states the Islamic conclusion on revelation's objective nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Islamic thought, revelation is not a subjective inner experience but a reception of an external, independent reality.

Core Idea
Revelation is objective, not subjective—it comes from outside the Prophet.

Buti summarizes a key conclusion of Islamic theology: revelation is not a product of the Prophet's mind or spiritual attainment. Instead, it is a genuine reception of a reality that exists independently of him. This short but dense statement sets the foundation for understanding the nature of prophethood and divine communication.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence once to appreciate its concise structure. Then read the English translation to grasp the meaning.
2
Identify the two key components
Notice that the definition has two parts: what revelation is (reception of an independent reality) and what it is not (not from the Prophet's acquisition or intellectual effort).
This contrast is central.
3
Consider the implication
Ask yourself: If revelation is external to the Prophet, what does that say about his role? He is a recipient, not a creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكانت النتيجة التي وصل إليها الفكر الإسلامي هي : اعتقاد أن الوحي إنما هو استقبال منه عليه الصلاة والسلام الحقيقة ذاتية مستقلة خارجة عن كيانه وشعوره الداخلي ، وبعيدة عن كسبه أو سلوكه الفكري أو العلمي .
The result reached by Islamic thought is: the belief that revelation, from him (peace be upon him), is a reception of an independent objective reality external to his being and inner feeling, and far from his acquisition or intellectual or scientific conduct.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents the Islamic conclusion regarding the nature of revelation. The author states that Islamic thought concludes that revelation is a reception of an independent reality that is external to the Prophet's own self and consciousness. It is not produced by his own acquisition or intellectual effort. The key point is that revelation is objective and distinct from the Prophet's subjective experience.

Key Terms
الوحي (revelation)
حقيقة ذاتية مستقلة (independent objective reality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Revelation is an inner psychological experience or the result of deep spiritual reflection.
Correction: Buti states it is a reception of an external independent reality, distinct from internal feelings or intellectual conduct.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the Islamic concept of revelation?
A) It is an internal psychological experience.
B) It is a reception of an independent objective reality external to the Prophet.
C) It is a type of intellectual inspiration.
D) It is a gradual spiritual unveiling.

Key Takeaway
Revelation in Islam is objectively received from God, not produced by the Prophet's own mind or effort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you truly approach it as an objective message from outside yourself, or do you unconsciously filter it through your own desires? What would change in your life if you never read a verse without asking: 'What is the external reality behind this command?'
?
The Prophet (ﷺ) did not 'acquire' revelation through his own intellect. Are there areas of your faith where you rely on your own reasoning more than the objective text? Will you commit to searching out a verse or hadith before acting on your own opinion today?
?
If revelation is completely independent of human psychology, then your feelings about a ruling do not change its truth. Which of God's commands have you been avoiding because it 'feels' too difficult or outdated? What step will you take this week to submit to that objective reality?

Western Methods and Theories on Revelation
Buti outlines the Western methodology for studying revelation and lists three resulting theories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Western methodological approach to studying revelation and the three secular theories it produced.

Core Idea
Western theories reduce revelation to human imagination, inspiration, or illness.

In this passage, Buti critiques the Western approach to revelation by first describing their method—treating revelation as a vague historical event and relying on intuition and conjecture. This method leads to three reductive theories, which the author presents in contrast to the Islamic understanding of revelation as divine communication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic text once through. Then read the English translation. Notice the two methodological steps and the three theories that follow.
Pay attention to the author's critical tone when describing these theories.
2
Identify the two methodological steps
The author describes two steps in the Western method: first, taking revelation as an ambiguous historical trace; second, using intuition and conjecture to interpret it. Find these in the text.
These steps are the foundation for the theories that follow.
3
List the three resulting theories
The passage presents three different conclusions: revelation as internal thought/psychological inspiration, as gradual spiritual illumination, and as epileptic seizures. Note each one and the phrasing used.
These theories are presented as distinct and divergent schools.
4
Reflect on the contrast with Islamic view
Consider how these theories differ from the Islamic belief that revelation is literal divine speech sent to prophets. Buti uses this contrast to highlight the inadequacy of the secular approach.
This sets the stage for subsequent discussion of the Islamic methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما المنهج الذي سلكه الغربيون في ذلك ، فهو : أولاً : أخذ كلمة ( الوحي ) على اعتبارها أثراً أو حادثة مبهمة خلفها التاريخ . ثانياً : إعمال الحدس والتخمين في استنتاج ما قد يدركه التوسم والوجدان والخيال من هذه الكلمة وكانت النتيجة التي توصلوا إليها في أمر الوحي على أعقاب ذلك ، أن اختلفوا فيه على مذاهب متفرقة . فمنهم من انتهى إلى أن الوحي إنما هو حركة فكرية داخلية أو نوع من الإلهام النفسي ، ومنهم من زعم أنه إشراق روحي جاء عن طريق الكشف التدريجي ، ومنهم من لم يجد أي غضاضة في أن يقرر أن الوحي لم يكن أكثر من نوبات صرع كانت تنتاب الرسول بين الحين والآخر .
As for the method followed by Westerners in that, it is: First: taking the word 'revelation' as an ambiguous trace or event left by history. Second: employing intuition and conjecture to deduce what insight, feeling, and imagination may perceive from this word. And the result they reached concerning revelation after that is that they differed on it into divergent schools. Some of them concluded that revelation is nothing but an internal intellectual movement or a type of psychological inspiration; some claimed that it is a spiritual illumination that came through gradual unveiling; and some saw no offense in declaring that revelation was no more than epileptic seizures that used to afflict the Messenger from time to time.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage describes the Western approach to studying revelation. The author states two methodological steps: treating revelation as a vague historical phenomenon, and then using intuition and conjecture to interpret it. This leads to three different theories: some see it as inner intellectual process or psychological inspiration; others as gradual spiritual illumination; and some even as epileptic fits. The passage contrasts these with the Islamic view.

Key Terms
الحدس (intuition)
التخمين (conjecture)
التوسم (insight)
الإلهام النفسي (psychological inspiration)
الكشف التدريجي (gradual unveiling)
نوبات صرع (epileptic seizures)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Western theories of revelation are essentially the same or one unified position.
Correction: The author presents three distinct and divergent schools, showing that Western scholars themselves disagree. They range from psychological inspiration to neurological disorder.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the Western theories of revelation mentioned by Buti?
A) Internal intellectual movement.
B) Psychological inspiration.
C) Gradual spiritual illumination.
D) Direct dictation from God.

Key Takeaway
The Western method of studying revelation, relying on intuition and conjecture, leads to reductive and conflicting theories that fail to recognize revelation as divine communication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face uncertainty about matters of faith, do you tend to rely on your own intuition and conjecture, or do you actively seek guidance from the Quran and Sunnah? What does your answer reveal about the source of your certainty?
?
Which of the three Western theories described here—psychological inspiration, gradual unveiling, or epileptic seizures—has the greatest potential to weaken your own conviction in the divine origin of the Quran? Why?
?
If you encountered a person who reduces the Prophet's revelation to a mere human experience, how would the author's critique of the Western method equip you to respond? What would you say to them based on this passage alone?

Buti's Critique of the Western Approach to Revelation
Buti criticizes Westerners for ignoring authentic transmitted reports and inventing interpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's critique of the Western approach to revelation and how it violates key Islamic epistemological principles.

Core Idea
Western thinkers fall into error by ignoring authentic transmitted reports and abandoning rational Islamic methods.

Buti argues that a fundamental methodological gap separates Western scholars from Islamic thinkers. He identifies two major failures: disregarding authentic prophetic reports (al-riwāya al-mutawātira) and abandoning key rational methods such as induction, the law of implication, and the argument from the greater. These failures lead to distorted portrayals of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. This will give you an overview of Buti's argument before diving into details.
Pay attention to the strong language Buti uses to describe Westerners' actions.
2
Identify the two main failures
Buti lists two specific failures: ignoring authentic mutawātir reports and inventing unsupported interpretations, and not adhering to induction, the law of implication, and qiyās al-awla.
These are the core of his methodological critique.
3
Understand the Islamic methods
Briefly review the meaning of istiqrā' (induction), qānūn al-iltizām (law of implication), and qiyās al-awla (argument from the greater). How do they relate to understanding revelation?
The commentary will explain these terms.
4
See the consequence
Notice how these failures lead to a contradictory and false image of the Prophet. Buti points out the absurdity of depicting the trustworthy Prophet as a liar and deceiver.
This highlights the real-world impact of methodological errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس ثمة مطمع في أن يلتقي هؤلاء ومفكرو الإسلام على صراط واحد من الفهم في الأمر ، إذ إن هؤلاء قد أسقطوا من اعتبارهم أمر الرواية والخبر وقيمتها العلمية سلباً وإيجاباً ، أي إنهم استجازوا لأنفسهم تجاهل الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة كما استجازوا في نفس الوقت اختراع تفسير لا يدعمه أي خبر أو رواية صحيحة . كما أنهم لم يلتزموا إطلاقاً بمنهج الاستقراء وما يثبته قانون الالتزام وقياس الأولى ، ولذلك جاز لهم أن يصوروا من محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام منذ اللحظة التي أوحي فيها إليه ، شخصية تتناقض كلياً مع شخصيته السابقة بل مع وقائع حياته المستمرة أيضاً ، وجاز لهم أن يجعلوا منه عليه الصلاة والسلام أعظم كذاب على الله بعد أن كان أعظم أمين وصادق مع الناس ، وأن يجعلوا منه أعظم ممثل ومخاتل ومدجل يصطنع الخوف وصفرة الوجه أمام خديجة من أمر ما قد رأى من الوحي مع أنه لم يكن يمارس في الواقع إلا بعض أفكار وإلهامات داخلية مجردة.
And there is no hope that these [Westerners] and the thinkers of Islam meet on one path of understanding in the matter, for these [Westerners] have dropped from their consideration the matter of narration and report and its scientific value positively and negatively, i.e., they permitted themselves to ignore the authentic mutawātir report while they also permitted themselves at the same time to invent an interpretation not supported by any report or authentic narration. Moreover, they absolutely did not adhere to the method of induction (istiqrā') and what the law of implication (qānūn al-iltizām) and the argument from the greater (qiyās al-awla) establish. Therefore, they allowed themselves to portray Muhammad (peace be upon him), from the moment revelation came to him, as a personality completely contradictory to his previous personality and even to the continuous facts of his life. They allowed themselves to make of him (peace be upon him) the greatest liar against God after he had been the greatest trustworthy and truthful person with people, and to make him the greatest actor, deceiver, and charlatan who feigned fear and pallor of face before Khadijah regarding something he had seen of revelation, when in reality he was only practicing some internal ideas and abstract inspirations.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the Western approach. The author argues that there is no common ground between Westerners and Islamic thinkers because Westerners disregard the value of authentic transmitted reports (al-riwāya al-ṣaḥīḥa al-mutawātira). They both ignore authentic narrations and invent interpretations without any support. Additionally, they abandon the methods of induction (istiqrā'), the law of implication (qānūn al-iltizām), and the argument from the greater (qiyās al-awla) — all of which are key Islamic epistemological tools. Consequently, they create a contradictory image of the Prophet: they depict him as a liar and deceiver after he was known as the most truthful, and they claim he feigned fear during revelation while reducing it to inner thoughts.

Key Terms
الرواية (narration)
الخبر (report)
المتواتر (mutawātir)
الاستقراء (induction)
قانون الالتزام (law of implication)
قياس الأولى (argument from the greater)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The critique is only about ignoring transmitted reports.
Correction: Buti also emphasizes the abandonment of specific rational methods (induction, law of implication, qiyas al-awla), not just the neglect of reports.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say Westerners disregarded that prevents them from reaching the same understanding as Islamic thinkers?
A) The use of reason.
B) The authentic transmitted reports and the methods of induction and analogy.
C) The importance of historical context.
D) The concept of miracles.

Key Takeaway
Buti's critique shows that Western approaches to revelation fail because they reject both transmitted knowledge and rational Islamic methodologies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the story of the first revelation, do you ever find yourself rationalizing it to fit a secular framework? Buti says Westerners invent interpretations unsupported by any report. Have you ever done that with a prophetic account? What would it mean for you to accept the reports as they are, even if they challenge your assumptions? Will you commit today to reading the Sira with trust in the transmitted reports?
?
The Prophet was the most truthful before revelation. Buti says Westerners turned him into the greatest liar. In your heart, have you ever entertained subtle doubts about the Prophet's integrity—perhaps questioning his motives or sincerity? If so, what does the consistency of his life demand from you? Will you actively counter that doubt by studying his established character and the proofs of his truthfulness?
?
Buti lists three Islamic methods: induction, implication, and argument from the greater. Are you using any of these when you study your faith, or do you rely on feelings, popular opinions, or Western criticisms? Which method do you most neglect? How can you deliberately practice it in your next Islamic study session?

Restoration of True Religion: Abraham to Muhammad
Buti narrates the history of true religion from Abraham to Muhammad's reform.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad restored the original religion of Abraham by preserving its pure elements and abolishing later innovations.

Core Idea
Muhammad restored, not replaced, the religion of Abraham.

Buti traces the continuity of true religion from Abraham through Ishmael's descendants, showing how corruption crept in over time. When Prophet Muhammad was sent, he did not start from scratch—he confirmed what remained of Abraham's way and removed the polytheistic additions. This lesson shows the principle of prophetic reform as restoration.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Let the narrative flow and key terms sink in before analysis.
Notice the quote from Quran 22:78 at the beginning.
2
Identify the principle of prophetic confirmation
The passage states that when a prophet is sent to a people with remnants of righteousness, he confirms rather than changes those practices. Find this principle and understand its rationale.
3
Trace the historical corruption and reform
Follow the story: from Ishmael's way to Amr ibn Luhay's innovations, then Muhammad's mission. Note what was kept and what was abolished.
The terms 'sa'ibah' and 'bahirah' refer to pre-Islamic pagan customs.
4
Reflect on the nature of Muhammad's mission
Ask yourself: What does this passage teach about the continuity of divine guidance? How does it challenge the idea that Muhammad brought a completely new religion?
This connects to the learning objective and core idea.

وإشاعة نورها . وذلك قوله تعالى ﴿ مِلَّةَ أبيكُمْ إبراهيم ﴾ [ الحج : ۷۸ ] ولما كان الأمر على ذلك ، وجب أن تكون أصول تلك الملة مسلمة وسننها مقررة . إذ النبي إذا بعث إلى قوم فيهم بقية سنة راشدة ، فلا معنى لتغييرها وتبديلها ، بل الواجب تقريرها لأنها أطوع لنفوسهم وأثبت عند الاحتجاج عليهم . وكان بنو إسماعيل توارثوا منهاج أبيهم إسماعيل فكانوا على تلك الشريعة إلى أن وجـد عمرو بن لحي فأدخل فيها أشياء برأيه الكاسد ، فضل وأضل . وشرع عبادة الأوثان وسيب السوائب وبحر البحائر . فهنالك بطل الدين واختلط الصحيح بالفاسد ، وغلب عليهم الجهل والشرك والكفر . فبعث الله سيدنا محمداً مقيماً لعوجهم ومصلحاً لفسادهم ، فنظر الله في شريعتهم فما كان منها موافقاً لمنهاج إسماعيل عليه السلام أو من شعائر الله أمر ببقائه ، وما كان منها تحريفاً أو فساداً أو من شعائر الشرك أو الكفر أبطله وسجل على إبطاله .
And spreading its light. That is His saying the Most High: "The religion of your father Abraham" [Al-Hajj: 78]. And when the matter was thus, it was necessary that the foundations of that religion be accepted and its traditions be established. For when the prophet is sent to a people among whom remains a righteous practice, there is no meaning to changing and altering it; rather, it is obligatory to establish it because it is more obedient to their souls and more established when arguing against them. And the Children of Ishmael inherited the way of their father Ishmael and they continued upon that law until Amr ibn Luhay appeared and introduced into it things by his corrupt opinion, and he went astray and led astray. And he instituted the worship of idols, and let free the Sa'ibah, and marked the Bahirah. Then the religion became void and the correct mixed with the corrupt, and ignorance, polytheism, and disbelief overcame them. So Allah sent our master Muhammad, straightening their crookedness and reforming their corruption. Then Allah looked at their law: whatever was in agreement with the way of Ishmael (peace be upon him) or among the rites of Allah, He commanded its preservation; and whatever was distortion, corruption, or among the rites of polytheism and disbelief, He abolished it and recorded its abolition.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative. The author begins by quoting the Quranic verse about the religion of Abraham. He argues that when a prophet is sent to a people who still have remnants of a righteous tradition, he does not change it but rather confirms it, because it is easier for the people to accept and stronger as evidence. He then recounts that the Children of Ishmael preserved the way of Ishmael until Amr ibn Luhay introduced innovations: idolatry, and practices like Sa'ibah and Bahirah (pre-Islamic customs). This led to corruption and the loss of true religion. Then Allah sent Prophet Muhammad to correct the deviations. Muhammad examined their practices: whatever was consistent with Ishmael's way or with Allah's commands he kept; whatever was distortion or polytheistic he abolished. Thus, the Prophet's mission was one of restoration, not complete innovation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet Muhammad abrogated all previous practices and established a completely new religion.
Correction: The passage shows that Muhammad preserved what was in agreement with the way of Ishmael and the rites of Allah, while only abolishing innovations and corruptions. His mission was one of restoration, not total replacement.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Muhammad do when sent to the people who had deviated from Ishmael's way?
A) He abolished all existing practices and established a completely new law.
B) He kept practices consistent with Ishmael's way and abolished corruptions.
C) He only changed the practices of Amr ibn Luhay.
D) He ignored the existing practices and focused on Monotheism only.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's mission was to restore the pure religion of Abraham, preserving its true elements and eliminating later corruptions.

The Unity of True Creed Across All Prophets
Asserts that true creed is one and the same from Adam to Muhammad, with Islam as its name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the essential creed—belief in God's oneness, transcendence, and the Hereafter—has remained unchanged from the first prophet to the last, and that this creed is called Islam.

Core Idea
From Adam to Muhammad, all prophets preached the one true creed: Islam.

This passage from Dr. al-Buti emphasizes a fundamental truth: divine revelation is not a series of contradictory messages but a single, consistent call to faith. The author shows that the core teachings of every prophet—tawhid, belief in the Last Day, and moral accountability—are identical. He then demonstrates from the Quran that this unified creed has always been known as Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's strong opening statement and the list of core beliefs.
The passage begins with a firm assertion that true creed cannot be multiple.
2
Identify the core beliefs
List the elements of the creed as mentioned: belief in God's existence, oneness, transcendence from defects, the Last Day, Reckoning, Paradise, Hell, etc.
These are the non-negotiable essentials of faith according to all prophets.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the two verses cited: Al-Anbiya 25 (monotheism) and Ash-Shura 13 (same religion ordained for all prophets). Note how they support the unity of the message.
The verses show that the core message is identical across prophets.
4
Reflect on the name 'Islam'
The author points out that Islam is not a new name but the ancient name of this creed. See how Abraham is called a Muslim (Al-Imran 67).
This connects the creed of all prophets to the term 'Islam'.
5
Consider the misconception
Some think different prophets brought different creeds. This passage corrects that: the essential belief system is identical, even if laws varied.
This is a key point in interfaith understanding.

Source Text

ثم إن هذه العقيدة لم يختلف مضمونها منذ بعثة آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى بعثة خاتم النبيين محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام، ومضمونها الذي تعاقب الرسل والأنبياء كلهم على الدعوة إليه هو : الإيمان بوجود الله ووحدانيته وتنزيهه عن كل ما لا يليق به من صفات النقص ، والإيمان باليوم الآخر والحساب والجنة والنار وما إلى ذلك . فكان كل رسول يدعو قومه إلى الاعتقاد بهذه الأمور ، وكان كل منهم يؤكد بذلك دعوة من بعث قبله ، ويبشر ببعثة من سيأتي بعده

ومثل قوله تعالى : وشَرَعَ لَكُم مِنَ الدِّين ما وَصَّى به نوحاً والذي أوحينا إليك ، وما وَصَّينا به إبراهيم وموسى وعيسى أن أقيموا الدِّينَ ولا تَتَفَرَّقوا فيه ﴾

·
وفي قوله تعالى عن سحرة فرعون : قالوا إنا إلى رَبِّنَا مُنْقَلِبُونَ وَما تَنقِمُ
True creed cannot be multiple and contradictory. Moreover, the content of this creed has not differed from the mission of Adam, peace be upon him, to the mission of the Seal of the Prophets Muhammad, peace be upon him. Its content, which all the messengers and prophets successively called to, is: belief in the existence of God, His oneness, and His transcendence above everything that does not befit Him of attributes of deficiency; belief in the Last Day, the Reckoning, Paradise, Hell, and so on. So every messenger called his people to believe in these matters, and each of them thereby affirmed the call of the one sent before him, and gave glad tidings of the mission of the one who would come after him. This is what God, Mighty and Majestic, clarified in His clear Book in many verses, such as His words: 'And We did not send any messenger before you except that We revealed to him that there is no god except Me, so worship Me' (Al-Anbiya: 25). And like His words: 'He has ordained for you of religion what He enjoined upon Noah and that which We have revealed to you, and what We enjoined upon Abraham, Moses, and Jesus: to establish the religion and not be divided therein' (Ash-Shura: 13). Rather, if you trace the verses of the Noble Quran, you will notice that the name 'Islam' was the ancient and permanent name of this creed. Consider, for example, His words: 'Abraham was neither a Jew nor a Christian, but he was a hanif, a Muslim, and he was not of the polytheists' (Al-Imran: 67). And in His words about the magicians of Pharaoh: 'They said: Indeed, to our Lord we will return. And what do you resent...'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage asserts that true creed cannot be multiple or contradictory. It argues that the content of the creed has remained unchanged from Adam to Muhammad. The core creed includes belief in God's existence, oneness, transcendence from deficiencies, and belief in the Hereafter, judgment, Paradise, Hell, etc. Every prophet invited his people to these same beliefs, confirming previous prophets and foretelling future ones. The author cites Quranic evidence: Al-Anbiya 25 shows that all prophets were sent with the message of monotheism; Ash-Shura 13 shows that God ordained the same religion for Noah, Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. Furthermore, the name 'Islam' is not a new label but the ancient and permanent name of this creed, as seen in Al-Imran 67 where Abraham is described as a Muslim. The passage ends with a partial verse from the story of Pharaoh's magicians (they say 'We return to our Lord and you resent...') which supports the idea of their faith in the same God.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Different prophets brought different or contradictory creeds.
Correction: The essential creed—belief in God's oneness, transcendence, and the Hereafter—is identical across all prophets. Only legal rulings (sharia) differed.

Key Takeaway
All prophets from Adam to Muhammad preached the same essential creed: belief in one God, His transcendence, and the Hereafter, and this creed is Islam.

The Unity of True Religion
Buti argues for unity of true religion and critiques 'heavenly religions'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the true religion is one and why the term 'heavenly religions' is logically inconsistent.

Core Idea
True religion is one because creed is a single report from Allah, impossible to contradict.

Many people today speak of 'the heavenly religions' as if there are multiple valid paths from God. But the Quran and sound reasoning tell us otherwise. The author uses two Quranic verses and a logical argument to show that the true religion has always been one, and the very nature of creed as a report prevents it from being multiple or contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Read the two verses from Surah al-A'raf and Surah Al-Imran that show earlier prophets' followers declaring themselves Muslims. Reflect on how they affirm the same faith.
Notice that both groups submit to Allah alone.
2
Understand the author's conclusion
The author concludes that the true religion is one, not multiple, and criticizes the common phrase 'heavenly religions' (plural).
3
Grasp the logical argument
The author explains that 'religion' means creed, and creed consists of reports (akhbar). A single report cannot be transmitted in contradictory forms and still be true.
This is the core logical move.
4
Reflect on the implication
If all prophets brought the same report, then their messages must agree. Therefore, there is only one true religion.
This resolves the apparent diversity into unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منا إلا أن آمنا بآياتِ رَبِّنَا لَمَّا جَاءَتِنا رَبَّنا أفرغ عَلَيْنَا صَبْراً وتَوَفَّنَا مُسلِمين ) 1 الأعراف : ١٢٥ - ١٢٦ ] وفي قوله تعالى عن حواريّي عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام : : ﴿ فَلَمَّا أَحَسَّ مِنْهُمُ الكفر قالَ مَن أنصاري إلى الله ؟ قالَ الحَوارِيُّونَ نَحْنُ أَنْصَارُ اللَّهِ آمَنَّا بالله واشهد بأنا مسلمون ﴾ [ آل عمران : ٥٢ ] . ومن هنا يتبين لك أن الدين الحق واحد لم يتعدد ، وأن كلمة ( الأديان السماوية ( التي تتكرر على ألسنة عوام الناس اليوم ، كلمة خاطئة فليس ثمة إلا دين حق سماوي واحد تعاقبت الأنبياء والرسل على الدعوة إليه والبعثة به • وكيف يمكن للدين الحق أن يتعدد أو يتخالف على ألسنة الأنبياء والمرسلين ، وإنما الدين يُطلق على العقيدة كما قد علمت ، ومقولات العقيدة تكون من قبيل الإخبار كما هو معلوم، والخبر الواحد لا يمكن أن يُنقل على أشكال ووجوه عديدة متخالفة ثم تكون كلها - مع ذلك ـ أخباراً صحيحة سماوية دائماً صادقة ؟
except that we believed in the signs of our Lord when they came to us. Our Lord, pour upon us patience and cause us to die as Muslims) 1 al-A'raf: 125-126] And in His saying – exalted is He – about the disciples of Jesus, peace be upon him: 'So when he sensed from them disbelief, he said, "Who are my helpers toward Allah?" The disciples said, "We are the helpers of Allah. We have believed in Allah and bear witness that we are Muslims."' [Al-Imran: 52]. From here it becomes clear to you that the true religion is one, not multiple, and that the phrase 'heavenly religions' which recurs on the tongues of common people today is an erroneous word. There is no true heavenly religion except one, to which prophets and messengers successively called and were sent. And how can the true religion be multiple or contradictory on the tongues of prophets and messengers? Rather, 'religion' is applied to creed, as you have learned, and the statements of creed are of the nature of reports, as is known. A single report cannot be transmitted in many diverse and contradictory forms, and then all of them be, despite that, correct, heavenly, ever truthful reports?
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage begins by quoting two Quranic verses: the first from Surah al-A'raf (7:126) where the magicians of Pharaoh declare their faith as Muslims, and the second from Surah Al-Imran (3:52) where the disciples of Jesus declare themselves Muslims. The author uses these to show that true faith is submission to Allah alone. He then argues that the true religion is one and has never been multiple. The common term 'heavenly religions' (plural) is mistaken; there is only one true divine religion to which all prophets called. He proves this by noting that 'religion' means creed, and creeds are statements of report (khabar). A single report cannot be transmitted in multiple contradictory forms and still be true. Therefore, the messages of all prophets must agree in creed.

Why Creed Stays the Same But Laws Change
The author states the principle that only legislation changes, not creed, and explains the wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that only legislation evolves over time while creed remains unchanged, and the wisdom behind this divine pattern.

Core Idea
Creed is fixed; laws adapt to changing human needs.

Many people wonder why some religious rulings seem to change from one prophet to another. The author begins by clarifying that what changes is only legislation (sharī‘a), not the core creed. This lesson explores the principle and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first sentence carefully to grasp the central claim: only legislation changes, not creed.
The Arabic word for legislation is التشريع.
2
Understand the wisdom
The author explains why legislation changes: it regulates life and must adapt to different times, places, and interests.
This is based on the idea of مصالح العباد (people's interests).
3
Distinguish creed and legislation
Notice that the passage contrasts legislation, which evolves, with creed, which is constant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجل ، إن الذي تطور وتغير مع الزمن وعن طريق بعثة الرسل والأنبياء ، إنما هو التشريع على اختلافه من عبادات وغيرها . والحكمة في ذلك أن التشريع ، أن إنما هو إقامة الأحكام التي يتوخى منها تنظيم حياة المجتمع والفرد ، وبديهي يكون للتطور الزمني ولاختلاف الأمم والأقوام أثر في تطور شرائعهم ، إذ إن فكرة التشريع من أساسها قائمة على ما تقتضيه مصالح العباد في دنياهم وآخرتهم ، وهذه المصالح كثيراً ما تختلف باختلاف الأزمنة والأمكنة فقد بعث موسى عليه السلام مثلاً إلى بني إسرائيل . وكان الشأن يقضي - بالنسبة لحال بني إسرائيل إذ ذاك - أن تكون شريعتهم شديدة قائمة في مجموعها على أساس العزائم لا الرخص . ولما مرت أزمنة وبعث فيهم سيدنا عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام . جاءهم بشريعة أسهل وأيسر ، وانظر في هذا إلى قول الله تعالى على لسان عيسى عليه السلام وهو يخاطب بني إسرائيل : فو ... وَمُصَدَّقاً لما بين يدي من التّوراة ، ولأحلَّ لَكُمْ بَعْض الذى حرّم عَلَيكُم ... ﴾ الآية [ آل عمران : ٥٠] . فقد بين لهم أنه فيما يتعلق بـأمـور العقيدة ، مصدق لما جاء في التوراة ومؤكد له ومجدد للدعوة إليه ، أما بالنسبة للتشريع وأحكام الحلال والحرام ، فقد كلف ببعض التغييرات وإيجاد بعض التسهيلات · ثم إن التشريعات من نوع الإنشاء ، فلا ضير في تغايرها مع الزمن ولا مانع عقلياً من تناسخها على مر الأحقاب والخلاصة أن بعثة كل رسول تتضمن عقيدة وتشريعاً فأما العقيدة ، فعمله بالنسبة لها ليس سوى تأكيد نفس العقيدة التي بعث بها من قبله دون أي تخالف أو تغيير . وأما التشريع فإن شريعة كل رسول ناسخة للشريعة السابقة إلا ما أيده التشريع المتأخر أو سكت عنه ، وذلك على مذهب من يقول : شريعة من قبلنا شريعة لنا ما لم يَردُّ ما يخالفها ✩ تلك وإذن ، فنحن حينما ندرس شؤون العقيدة وبراهينها ، إنما ندرس الحقائق التي ألزم الله عباده بالإيمان والاعتقاد بها منذ بعثة آدم إلى أن يرث الله الأرض ومن عليها . وتلك هي العلاقة بين العقيدة الإسلامية وكل مـا جـاء بـه الأنبياء والرسل عليهم صلاة الله وسلامه . وأهل الكتاب يعلمون هذه العلاقة ، ويعلمون وحدة الدين ، ويعلمون أن الأنبياء إنما جاؤوا ليصدق كل منهم الآخر
Yes, what developed and changed over time and through the sending of messengers and prophets is only legislation, in its various aspects such as acts of worship and others. The wisdom in that is that legislation is the establishment of rulings intended to regulate the life of society and the individual, and it is obvious that temporal development and differences among nations and peoples have an effect on the development of their laws, since the idea of legislation is fundamentally based on what the interests of people require in their worldly and religious affairs, and these interests often differ with differences of times and places. For example, Moses, peace be upon him, was sent to the Children of Israel. The situation required – regarding the state of the Children of Israel at that time – that their law be strict, based overall on strict obligations (al-azā'im) rather than concessions (al-rukhāṣ). When time passed and our master Jesus, peace be upon him, was sent among them, he brought them a law easier and more lenient. Look at this in the saying of Allah Almighty on the tongue of Jesus, peace be upon him, addressing the Children of Israel: '... and confirming what is before me of the Torah, and to make lawful for you some of what was forbidden to you...' the verse [Al-Imran: 50]. He made clear to them that regarding matters of creed, he was confirming what came in the Torah, affirming it, and renewing its call. As for legislation and rulings of the lawful and unlawful, he was charged with some changes and creating some facilitations. Then indeed, legislations are of the type of enactment, so there is no harm in their differing over time, nor is there any rational obstacle to their abrogation across ages. The conclusion is that the mission of every messenger includes creed and legislation. As for creed, his work regarding it is nothing but confirming the same creed with which the one before him was sent, without any variance or change. As for legislation, the law of every messenger abrogates the previous law, except what the later legislation confirms or remains silent about, according to the school of those who say: 'The law of those before us is a law for us unless something contradictory comes.' Therefore, when we study matters of creed and its proofs, we are studying the truths that Allah obligated His servants to believe in from the mission of Adam until Allah inherits the earth and those on it. That is the relationship between Islamic creed and everything brought by prophets and messengers, may Allah's prayers and peace be upon them. And the People of the Book know this relationship, and know the unity of religion, and know that the prophets only came to confirm each other.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage begins by affirming that what evolves over time is legislation, not creed. The author gives the wisdom: legislation is designed to regulate life and must adapt to changing times and places. He gives the example of Moses' strict law for the Israelites and Jesus' easier law. He quotes a verse (Q3:50) where Jesus says he confirms the Torah but makes some previously forbidden things lawful, showing that legislation can change. He then states that legislations are of the nature of enactment (inshā'), so they can differ and be abrogated. The conclusion is that each prophet's mission involves both creed (unchanging and confirmed) and legislation (may be abrogated by later prophets). Finally, he ties this to the study of Islamic creed: it is the same truths preached from Adam onward. The People of the Book should recognize this unity.

العزائم
الرخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That both creed and law change with every prophet.
Correction: Only legislation changes; creed remains the same throughout all prophets.

Checkpoint

A) Because creed changes too.
B) Because it must adapt to different times and interests of people.
C) Because prophets had different messages.
D) Because God changes His mind.

Key Takeaway
Legislation evolves to serve changing human interests, while creed remains fixed across all prophets.

What would it mean for your relationship with Allah if you believed both creed and law could change?

Moses and Jesus: Same Creed, Different Laws
The author illustrates legislative change with the example of Moses and Jesus, citing a Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how the examples of Moses and Jesus illustrate that creed is confirmed while legislation can be eased.

Core Idea
Prophets confirm the unchanging creed but adjust laws to suit their people.

The author now gives a concrete historical example: Moses brought a strict law for the Israelites, and later Jesus confirmed the same creed but made some things lawful. This lesson examines that example and the Quranic verse.

Guided Path

Read the example of Moses and Jesus

2

The author concludes that each prophet's mission includes both creed (confirmed) and legislation (may be abrogated).
The final paragraph ties this to the study of Islamic creed.

Unity of Creed and Abrogation of Sharia
Author explains the unity of creed and abrogation of sharia using Jesus' example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all prophets share a single, unchanging creed while their laws (sharia) can abrogate one another, and why this distinction is crucial for Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Creed is one; laws differ and abrogate.

This passage from Ramadan al-Buti clarifies a foundational principle: every prophet brought the same core beliefs, but the legal rulings (halal/haram) could change over time. Using Jesus' own words from the Quran, the author shows that Jesus confirmed the Torah's creed while making some lawful what was previously forbidden. This distinction between creed (ʿaqīdah) and legislation (tashrīʿ) is essential for understanding the unity of all divine messages and the wisdom behind abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Notice how the author uses a Quranic verse as evidence and then builds his argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'التشريعات من نوع الإنشاء' – legislations are of the type of creation/innovation.
2
Identify the two key distinctions
The passage distinguishes between creed (ʿaqīdah) and legislation (tashrīʿ). Find where the author explains each and how they relate to the mission of prophets.
3
Understand the role of Jesus
Look at how the author interprets the verse from Surah Al Imran (3:50). What does Jesus confirm? What does he change? This illustrates the principle.
Jesus confirms the Torah's creed but makes some things lawful – this is abrogation of legislation, not creed.
4
Connect to the broader conclusion
The author concludes that Islamic creed is the same truth from Adam to the end. Reflect on how this relates to the People of the Book and their differences.
The final Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:19) reinforces that true religion is Islam, and differences arose from transgression.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you have grasped the core idea: what does a new prophet do regarding creed?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلام. جاءهم بشريعة أسهل وأيسر، وانظر في هذا إلى قول الله تعالى على لسان عيسى عليه السلام وهو يخاطب بني إسرائيل: فو ... وَمُصَدَّقاً لما بين يدي من التوراة، ولأحلَّ لَكُمْ بَعْضَ الَّذِي حُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ ... الآية [آل عمران: ٥٠]. فقد بيَّن لهم أنه فيما يتعلق بأمور العقيدة، مصدق لما جاء في التوراة ومؤكد له ومجدد للدعوة إليه، أما بالنسبة للتشريع وأحكام الحلال والحرام، فقد كُلِّف ببعض التغييرات وإيجاد بعض التسهيلات.

ثم إن التشريعات من نوع الإنشاء، فلا ضير في تغايرها مع الزمن ولا مانع عقلياً من تناسخها على مر الأحقاب.

والخلاصة أن بعثة كل رسول تتضمن عقيدة وتشريعاً. فأما العقيدة، فعمله بالنسبة لها ليس سوى تأكيد نفس العقيدة التي بعث بها من قبله دون أي تخالف أو تغيير. وأما التشريع فإن شريعة كل رسول ناسخة للشريعة السابقة إلا ما أيده التشريع المتأخر أو سكت عنه، وذلك على مذهب من يقول: شريعة من قبلنا شريعة لنا ما لم يرد ما يخالفها.

وإذن، فنحن حينما ندرس شؤون العقيدة وبراهينها، إنما ندرس الحقائق التي ألزم الله عباده بالإيمان والاعتقاد بها منذ بعثة آدم إلى أن يرث الله الأرض ومن عليها. وتلك هي العلاقة بين العقيدة الإسلامية وكل ما جاء به الأنبياء والرسل عليهم صلاة الله وسلامه. وأهل الكتاب يعلمون هذه العلاقة، ويعلمون وحدة الدين، ويعلمون أن الأنبياء إنما جاؤوا ليصدق كل منهم الآخر فيما بعث به، وما كانوا ليتفرقوا إلى عقائد متباينة مختلفة، ولكنهم اختلفوا وتفرقوا فيما بينهم، واختلقوا على الأنبياء ما لم يقولوه على الرغم مما جاءهم من العلم في ذلك، بغياً بينهم. وصدق الله العظيم إذ يقول في محكم تبيانه: {إن الدين عند الله الإسلام وما اختلف الذين أوتوا الكتاب إلا من بعد ما جاءهم العلم بغياً بينهم ومن يكفر بآيات الله فإن الله سريع الحساب} [آل عمران: ١٩].
And peace. He came to them with an easier and more lenient law, and look at this to the saying of Allah the Exalted on the tongue of Jesus, peace be upon him, as he addressed the Children of Israel: ... 'And confirming what is before me of the Torah, and to make lawful for you some of what was forbidden to you...' verse [Al Imran: 50]. He made clear to them that regarding matters of creed, he is confirming what came in the Torah, affirming it, and renewing the call to it. As for legislation and rulings of halal and haram, he was tasked with some changes and making some facilitations. Then indeed legislations are of the type of innovation, so there is no harm in them differing with time, nor any rational obstacle to their abrogation over the ages. And the conclusion is that the mission of every messenger includes creed and legislation. As for creed, his work concerning it is nothing but affirming the same creed sent with the one before him, without any contradiction or change. As for legislation, the law of each messenger abrogates the previous law except what the later legislation affirmed or remained silent about, and that is according to the position of those who say: The law of those before us is a law for us unless something contradictory comes. Therefore, when we study the matters of creed and its proofs, we are studying the truths that Allah obligated His servants to believe and have faith in from the mission of Adam until Allah inherits the earth and those on it. And that is the relationship between Islamic creed and everything brought by the prophets and messengers, may Allah's prayers and peace be upon them. And the People of the Book know this relationship, and know the unity of the religion, and know that the prophets only came to each confirm the other in what he was sent with, and they would not have split into differing and contradictory creeds. But they differed and split among themselves, and fabricated against the prophets what they did not say, despite the knowledge that came to them in that, out of transgression among themselves. And Allah the Great spoke truth when He said in His clear revelation: {Indeed, the religion with Allah is Islam. And those who were given the Scripture did not differ except after knowledge had come to them, out of transgression among themselves. And whoever disbelieves in the verses of Allah, then indeed Allah is swift in account} [Al Imran: 19].
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the relationship between the messages of all prophets, clarifying that creed is universal and unchanging while legislation is subject to abrogation. The author begins by citing Jesus’ statement in the Quran (Al Imran 3:50) where Jesus declares he confirms the Torah and makes some things lawful that were previously forbidden. This shows that Jesus’ role regarding creed was confirmatory and renewing, while regarding legal rulings he made some changes and facilitations. The author then explains that legislations (tashriʿat) are of the type of 'insha'' (creation/innovation) – meaning they are divinely instituted and thus can differ over time without rational objection; abrogation (naskh) is rationally possible across ages. He then summarizes: every messenger brings both creed and legislation. For creed, each messenger merely reaffirms the same creed as his predecessor without any discrepancy. For legislation, each messenger’s law abrogates the previous law except where the later law affirms it or remains silent about it, following the principle that the law of those before us is binding unless abrogated. The author then extends this to the study of Islamic creed: when we study creedal matters and their proofs, we are studying the truths that Allah has obligated since Adam until the end of time. This is the relationship between Islamic creed and all prophetic messages. The People of the Book (Jews and Christians) know this unity of religion and that prophets came to confirm each other, but they differed among themselves out of transgression, fabricating things against the prophets despite having knowledge. The passage concludes with Quranic support (Al Imran 3:19) affirming that the only true religion is Islam, and that the People of the Book only differed after knowledge came to them out of transgression.

Key Terms
عقيدة (ʿaqīdah) creed
تشريع (tashrīʿ) legislation
نسخ (naskh) abrogation
إنشاء (inshāʾ) creation/innovation
رسول (rasūl) messenger
نبي (nabī) prophet
وحدة الدين (waḥdat al-dīn) unity of religion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all religions are essentially the same in every aspect, including laws and rituals.
Correction: This passage clarifies that only the core creed (beliefs about God, prophethood, etc.) is identical across prophets; the laws (sharia) differ and abrogate one another.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the role of a new messenger concerning the creed of previous messengers?
A) He may change or alter the creed according to new circumstances.
B) He only reaffirms and confirms the same creed without any change.
C) He brings a completely new creed abrogating the old.
D) He can add new articles of faith to the creed.

Key Takeaway
All prophets share one unchanging creed, but each prophet's law (sharia) may abrogate or modify previous laws, reflecting the unity of religion and diversity of legislation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The People of the Book knew the truth but differed out of transgression (baghy). Are there areas of your life where you know what Allah wants from you, yet you resist or rationalize because of pride or social pressure? What would it take for you to submit fully, even if it costs you comfort or reputation?

Conclusive Proofs Against False Interpretations of Revelation
Buti enumerates four refuted explanations of revelation and three proof methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that rational investigation compels certainty that revelation was not a subjective feeling, a lie, taught by someone, or from jinn, and you will learn the three logical methods used to prove this.

Core Idea
Revelation is proven not to be subjective, false, taught, or demonic — using entailment, analogy, and induction.

After establishing the prophet's truthfulness, Buti now confronts alternative explanations of revelation that skeptics might propose. He synthesizes four false possibilities and shows that rational proofs — not just faith — eliminate them. In this passage, he summarizes the conclusion and outlines the logical methods that will be fully detailed later.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four negations
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. List the four things Buti says we are compelled to be certain are false about revelation.
The negations are: not internal feeling, not a lie, not taught by a human, not from jinn.
2
Identify the three proof methods
Find the three methods Buti mentions as the basis for certainty: entailment, primary analogical reasoning, and complete induction. Note their Arabic terms.
These methods will be explained in detail later; here just note them.
3
Understand the nature of the certainty
Notice that Buti uses the word 'نضطر إلى القطع' (we are compelled to certainty). Reflect on why these methods yield conclusive rational proof.
This is a strong epistemological claim.
4
Connect to the broader structure
Buti says the full elaboration belongs to the section on prophethood. Why do you think he gives this overview here? How does it prepare for later proofs?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن عندما نحقق في ظاهرة الوحي على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس الأولى والاستقراء الدقيق التام. وأنت تعلم أن المكان الملائم لتفصيل هذه البراهين وعرضها عند البحث في قسم النبوات آت قريباً إن شاء الله، وإنما نحن هنا نصور خطوات البحث ومراحله وكيفية التدرج من الأدنى إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها.
And when we investigate the phenomenon of revelation on this basis, we are compelled to be certain that revelation was not an internal feeling that occurred to Muhammad (peace and prayer be upon him), and that he did not lie to people in what he said, and that no one from his era was hiding behind him to teach him this which he says is revelation from God, and that it cannot be the whisper of a jinn or devils; we are compelled to be certain of negating these possibilities by the proof of entailment, primary analogical reasoning, and precise complete induction. And you know that the appropriate place for detailing these proofs and presenting them is in the section on prophethood coming soon, God willing, and here we only depict the steps of research and its stages and how to ascend from the lower to the end that we will discover.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage provides the conclusion of the rational investigation into revelation. Buti states that when we properly investigate revelation, we are forced to reject four possibilities: that it was subjective feeling, that Muhammad lied, that someone taught him, or that it was from jinn. The proof for this rejection is based on three methods: necessary entailment (التلازم), primary analogical reasoning (القياس الأولى), and complete induction (الاستقراء التام). He notes that the full elaboration belongs to the later section on prophethood; here he is only outlining the research stages.

الاستقراء التام
وسوسة
النبوات

Correction: Buti argues that rational investigation compels certainty that it was not an internal feeling, using entailment, primary analogy, and complete induction.

So if you realize this truth, after your faith in Allah, Mighty and Majestic, then you must inevitably engage in research concerning what is incumbent upon you of duty and responsibility towards your great Creator, who did not limit Himself to making you just a creature among His many creatures, but made you master of these creatures and cast to you the reins of their subjugation and the keys to much of them; so that when you know your function in the universe, you roll up your sleeves for serious effort to execute the function and to participate with all the components in carrying out the works and tasks assigned to each.

Definition of Nubuwwa and Risala and Their Distinction
Buti defines nubuwwa and risala, explains the difference, and presents the scholarly debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct meanings of nubuwwa and risala, how they describe different relationships, and the scholarly debate about their synonymy.

Core Idea
Nubuwwa is the prophet's link to Allah; risala is his link to the people.

This lesson establishes the foundational definitions of prophethood and messengerhood. Before we can discuss the role of prophets, we need a precise understanding of what these terms mean and how they relate. Buti begins by deriving the terms from their linguistic roots and then explains the two relationships they describe—one vertical, one horizontal. He also introduces a scholarly discussion about whether every prophet is a messenger and vice versa, reminding us that not all theological questions have a single agreed answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation. Note the root n-b-a and r-s-l.
2
Understand the definitions
Identify how Buti defines nubuwwa (reception of news from Allah) and risala (commission to convey). Notice the use of 'al-wahy' and 'al-inba'.
Focus on the relationship each term describes.
3
Grasp the distinction
The passage explains that nubuwwa is the relationship with Allah, and risala is the relationship with people. This makes nubuwwa more noble. Find that sentence.
4
Engage with the debate
Buti introduces a scholarly disagreement: are nubuwwa and risala synonyms or distinct? Note the position of al-Qadi 'Iyad that they are synonyms but with different perspectives.
This is an ijtihadi matter, not definitive creed.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولا تحقيق معنى النبوة والرسالة وتعريف كل منهما النبوّة ، مأخوذة من النبأ بمعنى الخبر ، ومعنـاهـا وصول خبر من الله بطريق الوحي إلى من اختاره من عباده لتلقي ذلك ، فالكلمة إذا تفسير للعلاقة التي بين النبي والخالق جل جلاله ، وهي علاقة الوحي والإنباء • والرسالة ، تعني تكليف الله أحد عباده بإبلاغ الآخرين بشرع أو حكم معين . فالكلمة إذا تفسير للعلاقة التي بين النبي وسائر الناس . وهي . علاقة البعث والإرسال · فإذا لاحظت في النبي الحالة التي بينه وبين ، عز وجل ، فهي النبوة . وإذا لاحظت حالته التي بينه وبين الناس فهي الرسالة . ومن هنا كانت النبوة أشرف من الرسالة . إذ كانت الرسالة بياناً لصلة ما بين الرسول والناس ، وكانت النبوة بياناً لصلة ما بينه وبين ربه عز وجل . الفرق بين النبوة والرسالة : وها هنا بحث اجتهادي ، غير داخل في الحقائق القطعية المتفق عليها ، ولذا وقع فيه الخلاف بين العلماء ، وهو : هل النبي والرسول كلمتان تطلقان على مدلول واحد ، أم يطلقان على مدلولين مختلفين حتى إنه يجوز أن يكون الإنسان نبياً ولا يكون رسولاً ؟ العلماء إلى أن الكلمتين مترادفتان وأنها ذات مدلول واحد ذهب طائفة من ، فكل نبي يسمى رسولاً ، وكل رسول نبياً ، غير أنه يسمى رسولاً بالنظر إلى ما بينه وبين الناس ، ويسمى نبياً بالنظر إلى ما بينه وبين الله . وكلاهما متلازمان ، وممن ذهب هذا المذهب القاضي عياض من المالكية وغيره .
First: Ascertaining the meaning of prophethood and messengerhood and defining each. Prophethood (nubuwwa) is derived from naba' meaning news, and its meaning is the arrival of news from God by way of revelation to whomever He has chosen from His servants to receive that. So the word thus explains the relationship between the prophet and the Creator, Exalted is His Majesty — a relationship of revelation and informing. Messengerhood (risala) means God's charging one of His servants with conveying to others a particular law or ruling. So the word thus explains the relationship between the prophet and the rest of people — a relationship of sending and being sent. So if you observe in the prophet the state between him and God Almighty, that is prophethood. And if you observe his state between him and the people, that is messengerhood. Hence, prophethood is more noble than messengerhood, since messengerhood is an expression of the connection between the messenger and the people, while prophethood is an expression of the connection between him and his Lord Almighty. The difference between prophethood and messengerhood: And here there is an ijtihadi discussion, not included among the decisive agreed-upon truths, and therefore disagreement occurred among scholars: Are the two words 'prophet' and 'messenger' applied to a single meaning, or are they applied to two different meanings such that it is possible for a person to be a prophet but not a messenger? Some scholars held that the two words are synonymous and have a single meaning, so every prophet is called a messenger and every messenger is a prophet; however, he is called a messenger with respect to what is between him and the people, and called a prophet with respect to what is between him and God. Both are inseparable. Among those who held this view is al-Qadi 'Iyad of the Malikis and others.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage defines the key terms nubuwwa (prophethood) and risala (messengerhood) and clarifies their relationship. The author begins by giving the linguistic derivation of nubuwwa from naba' (news), and defines it as the reception of divine revelation by a chosen servant. Risala is defined as the commission to convey a specific law or ruling to others. The author then explains that these two terms describe two different relationships: nubuwwa is the vertical relationship between the prophet and God, while risala is the horizontal relationship between the prophet and the people. From this, it follows that nubuwwa is more noble because it directly relates to God. The author then presents a scholarly debate: are these terms synonymous or distinct? Some scholars, like al-Qadi 'Iyad, hold that they are synonymous but describe different aspects — every prophet is a messenger and vice versa, but the designation depends on perspective. The author notes this is an ijtihadi matter, not a definitive creedal issue.

Key Terms
النبوة (al-nubuwwa)
الرسالة (al-risala)
الوحي (al-wahy)
الإنباء (al-inba')
الإرسال (al-irsal)
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think nubuwwa and risala are completely independent and unrelated concepts, such that a person could be a prophet without being a messenger or vice versa.
Correction: The passage shows that nubuwwa and risala describe two interrelated aspects of the same prophetic role: nubuwwa concerns the relationship with Allah (receiving revelation), and risala concerns the relationship with people (conveying the message). Even in the debate over synonymy, both sides agree that these aspects are inseparable in the prophets.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does nubuwwa primarily describe?
A) The prophet's relationship with his community
B) The prophet's relationship with Allah through revelation
C) The act of conveying a message
D) The prophet's miracles

Key Takeaway
Nubuwwa is the reception of divine revelation, forming a direct link to Allah; risala is the commission to convey that revelation to people, forming a link to humanity.

النبوّة، مأخوذة من النبأ بمعنى الخبر، ومعناها وصول خبر من الله بطريق الوحي إلى من اختاره من عباده لتلقي ذلك، فالكلمة إذاً تفسير للعلاقة التي بين النبي والخالق جل جلاله، وهي علاقة الوحي والإنباء. والرسالة، تعني تكليف الله أحد عباده بإبلاغ الآخرين بشرع أو حكم معين. فالكلمة إذاً تفسير للعلاقة التي بين النبي وسائر الناس. وهي علاقة البعث والإرسال. فإذا لاحظت في النبي الحالة التي بينه وبين الله عز وجل، فهي النبوة. وإذا لاحظت حالته التي بينه وبين الناس فهي الرسالة. ومن هنا كانت النبوة أشرف من الرسالة. إذ كانت الرسالة بياناً لصلة ما بين الرسول والناس، وكانت النبوة بياناً لصلة ما بينه وبين ربه عز وجل. الفرق بين النبوة والرسالة: وها هنا بحث اجتهادي، غير داخل في الحقائق القطعية المتفق عليها، ولذا وقع فيه الخلاف بين العلماء، وهو: هل النبي والرسول كلمتان تطلقان على مدلول واحد، أم يطلقان على مدلولين مختلفين حتى إنه يجوز أن يكون الإنسان نبياً ولا يكون رسولاً؟ العلماء ذهب طائفة من إلى أن الكلمتين مترادفتان وأنها ذات مدلول واحد، فكل نبي يسمى رسولاً، وكل رسول نبياً، غير أنه يسمى رسولاً بالنظر إلى ما بينه وبين الناس، ويسمى نبياً بالنظر إلى ما بينه وبين الله. وكلاهما متلازمان، وممن ذهب هذا المذهب القاضي عياض من المالكية وغيره. وذهب كثيرون إلى أن بينهما عموماً وخصوصاً مطلقاً، إذ النبي هو من أوحي إليه بأمر من الله، سواء كلف بتبليغه أم لا، فإن كلف بتبليغه كأن أوحي إليه بشرع أو كتاب إلى عامة الناس، فهو رسول أيضاً. وعلى هذا، فكل رسول نبي، إذ الرسالة إلى الناس فرع عن النبوة من الله، وليس كل نبي رسولاً، إذ قد يكون موحى إليه، دون تكليف له بالتبليغ. ولكل من الفريقين أدلة من ظاهر الكتاب والسنة، ولسنا بحاجة في هذا الصدد إلى عرض شيء منها، أو إلى إطالة البحث بالترجيح. إذ الخطب يسير ما دام البحث كما قلنا لا يتعلق بشيء من قواطع الدين وضرورياته، بل من الفروع الاجتهادية المحتملة.
Prophethood (al-nubuwwa) is derived from al-naba' meaning news, and its meaning is the arrival of news from God by way of revelation (al-waḥy) to whom He chooses from His servants to receive that. So the word is an interpretation of the relationship between the prophet (al-nabī) and the Creator, Exalted is His Majesty, and it is the relationship of revelation and announcement. And messengerhood (al-risāla) means God's entrusting one of His servants to convey to others a specific law or command. So the word is an interpretation of the relationship between the prophet and the rest of people, and it is the relationship of sending and delegation. So if in the prophet you observe the state between him and God, Mighty and Majestic, then it is prophethood. And if you observe his state between him and people, then it is messengerhood. Hence prophethood is nobler than messengerhood, since messengerhood is an explanation of the link between the messenger and people, and prophethood is an explanation of the link between him and his Lord, Mighty and Majestic. The difference between prophethood and messengerhood: Here is an ijtihadī discussion, not included among the definitive agreed-upon realities, and therefore disagreement occurred among scholars, namely: Are 'prophet' and 'messenger' two terms applied to one meaning, or are they applied to two different meanings such that it is possible for a person to be a prophet without being a messenger? A group of scholars held that the two terms are synonymous and have one meaning: every prophet is called a messenger, and every messenger a prophet, except that he is called messenger with regard to what is between him and people, and called prophet with regard to what is between him and God. Both are inseparable. Among those who held this opinion is al-Qāḍī 'Iyāḍ of the Mālikīs and others. And many held that between them there is general and specific absolute, for the prophet is one to whom something is revealed by God, whether he is charged to convey it or not, and if he is charged to convey it, such as if a law or book is revealed to him for the general people, then he is also a messenger. And on this, every messenger is a prophet, since messengership to people is a branch of prophethood from God, and not every prophet is a messenger, for he may receive revelation without being charged to convey. Each of the two groups has evidence from the apparent meaning of the Book and the Sunna, and we are not in need in this regard to present any of it or to prolong discussion by weighting. For the matter is easy as long as the discussion, as we said, does not pertain to any of the definitive matters of religion and its necessities, but rather to possible ijtihadī branches.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage defines prophethood (nubuwwa) and messengerhood (risāla) and explains the scholarly difference between them. The author begins by providing the linguistic derivation of nubuwwa from naba' (news), and defines it as the arrival of news from God through revelation to a chosen servant. He then defines risāla as God's commissioning a servant to convey a specific law or command to others. He explains that nubuwwa describes the relationship between the prophet and God, while risāla describes the relationship between the prophet and people. Therefore, nubuwwa is nobler because it concerns direct connection with God. Then the author introduces a scholarly debate: are the terms 'prophet' and 'messenger' synonymous or distinct? He presents two opinions. The first opinion, held by al-Qāḍī 'Iyāḍ and others, is that the terms are synonymous, with the difference only in perspective: 'prophet' regarding God, 'messenger' regarding people. The second opinion, held by many, is that they are in a general-specific relationship: a prophet is anyone who receives revelation, but a messenger is a prophet who is commanded to convey that revelation. On this view, every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger. The author notes that this is an ijtihadī issue, not a definitive matter of religion, so he does not need to weigh the evidence or prolong the discussion.

رسالة
وحي
نبي
رسول
