The Prophet's Fear as Proof of External Origin
Buti uses the Prophet's involuntary fear to argue that revelation was not self-induced.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's involuntary fear and terror are strong evidence that revelation came from an external source, not from his own thoughts or gradual spiritual development.

Core Idea
True revelation surprises; counterfeit visions do not terrify.

We've seen that the Qur'an's literary miracle points to divine origin. Now Buti offers a second, psychological argument: the Prophet's own fear. When revelation first came, the Prophet was not calm or expectant—he was terrified. This involuntary reaction cannot be faked and contradicts any theory of self-induced revelation. Let's trace his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice how Buti describes the Prophet's fear as immediate and overwhelming.
Pay attention to the physical details: trembling, paleness, rushing home.
2
Identify the two main arguments
Buti uses two strands: (1) gradual thought does not produce sudden terror, and (2) fear is involuntary and cannot be pretended. Find where each appears.
The second argument uses a certain syllogism (qiyās yaqīnī).
3
Understand the certain syllogism
Buti claims that by induction, all cases of gradual meditation result in calm, not fear. Therefore, the Prophet's fear could not come from meditation.
This is an inductive argument based on observation of human psychology.
4
Reflect on the impossibility of faking
Even if we suppose the Prophet could deceive, his known character of truthfulness makes it impossible. Fear is an involuntary emotion that shows the experience was real.
The argument also guards against the idea that the fear was a sign of weakness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد داخله الخوف والرعب مما سمع ورأى ، حتى إنه قطع خلوته في الغار وأسرع عائداً إلى البيت يرجف فؤاده، لكي يتضح لكل مفكر عاقل أن رسول الله لم يكن متشوقاً للرسالة التي سيدعى إلى حملها وبثها في العالم ، وأن ظاهرة الوحي هذه لم تأت منسجمة أو متممة لشيء مما قد كان يتصوره أو يخطر في باله وإنما طرأت طروءاً مثيراً على حياته ، وفوجئ بها ( بالرسالة ) دون أي توقع سابق ولا شك أن هذا ليس شأن من يتدرج في التأمل والتفكير إلى أن تتكون في نفسه - بطريقة الكشف التدرجي المستمر - عقيدة يؤمن بالدعوة إليها ثم إن شيئاً من حالات الإلهام أو حديث النفس أو الإشراق الروحي أو التأملات العلوية لا يستدعي الخوف والرعب واصفرار اللون . يدل على ذلك القياس اليقيني القائم على استقراء الحالات وجميع الظروف المشابهة وليس ثمة أي انسجام بين التدرج في التفكير والتأمل من ناحية ، ومفاجأة الخوف والرعب من ناحية أخرى ، وإلا للزم من ذلك أن يعيش جميع المفكرين والمتأملين نهباً لدفعات من الرعب والخوف المفاجئة المتلاحقة وأنت خبير أن الخوف والرعب ورجفان الجسم وتغير اللون ـ كل ذلك من الانفعالات القسرية التي لا سبيل إلى اصطناعها والتمثيل بها ، حتى لو فرضنا إمكان صدور المخادعة والتمثيل منه عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وفرضنا المستحيل من انقلاب طباعه المعروفة قبل البعثة من الصدق والأمانة إلى عكس ذلك تماماً
And fear and terror entered him from what he heard and saw, so much so that he broke his seclusion in the cave and hastened back home with his heart trembling, so that it becomes clear to every rational thinker that the Messenger of God was not eager for the message to which he would be called to carry and spread in the world, and that this phenomenon of revelation did not come consistent with or completing anything he might have imagined or occurred to his mind, but rather it occurred as an exciting occurrence in his life, and he was surprised by it (the message) without any prior expectation. And there is no doubt that this is not the state of one who progresses gradually in meditation and thought until there forms in himself—by way of continuous gradual unveiling—a belief he is called to. Moreover, nothing of the states of inspiration (ilhām) or self-talk or spiritual illumination or lofty meditations necessitates fear, terror, and pallor. That is indicated by the certain syllogism (al-qiyās al-yaqīnī) based on induction of cases and all similar circumstances. There is no harmony between gradual thought and meditation on the one hand, and the surprise of fear and terror on the other. Otherwise, it would necessarily follow that all thinkers and meditators would be prey to successive sudden waves of terror and fear. And you are well aware that fear, terror, trembling of the body, and change of color—all of these are involuntary emotions (infiʿālāt qasriyya) that cannot be feigned or pretended, even if we suppose the possibility of deceit and pretension from him, peace and blessings be upon him, and suppose the impossible transformation of his well-known character before the mission from truthfulness and trustworthiness to the complete opposite of that.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument for the external origin of revelation, based on the Prophet's psychological state. Buti describes the Prophet's intense fear and terror after the encounter, causing him to rush home trembling. The purpose is to show that the Prophet was not expecting or desiring this mission (risāla); it came as a complete surprise. This contradicts any theory that revelation emerged from prolonged meditation (tadrīj fī al-tafkīr) or internal spiritual illumination (ishrāq rūḥī). Buti argues that such gradual internal processes do not produce sudden fear and terror. He supports this with a certain syllogism (qiyās yaqīnī) based on induction: all similar cases of gradual thought lead to calm, not terror. If gradual meditation caused such fear, all thinkers would experience it. Furthermore, the physical symptoms—trembling, pallor—are involuntary (qasriyya) and cannot be faked. Even if one hypothetically assumed the Prophet could deceive, his well-known character of truthfulness (ṣidq) and trustworthiness (amāna) before the mission makes that impossible. Hence, the fear is genuine proof that the revelation was an external shock, not an internal development.

Key Terms
خوف
رعب
انفعالات قسرية
قياس يقيني
تدرج في التفكير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's fear shows he was weak or that revelation must be accompanied by calm confidence.
Correction: Buti shows that the fear proves the revelation was a genuine external shock, not a product of his own mind. Involuntary fear is evidence of authenticity, not weakness.

Checkpoint
Why does Buti argue that the Prophet's fear cannot be a sign of internal revelation?
A) Because internal meditation always produces joy.
B) Because involuntary emotions cannot be faked and are inconsistent with gradual thought.
C) Because the Prophet was known to be fearless.
D) Because fear only occurs in external events.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's involuntary fear, which cannot be faked and is inconsistent with gradual meditation, proves that revelation came as an external shock, not from his own mind.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was terrified by the revelation. Have you ever been so confronted by a truth from Allah that it shook you physically and emotionally? What truth have you been avoiding because it would disturb your comfort and routine? This lesson demands you ask: Am I open to being surprised by God, or do I only seek spiritual experiences that I control?
?
If the Prophet's fear was involuntary and could not be faked, then the message he delivered is undeniably from outside himself. Do you treat the Qur'an as a direct, external command from God that overrides your own desires, or do you sometimes reduce it to a set of good suggestions you can pick and choose from? Your answer determines whether you have truly submitted.
?
Buti says gradual meditation leads to calm, not terror. Many today seek spiritual highs through meditation, yoga, or self-reflection, but these often bring peace, not the awe that accompanies divine revelation. Have you ever felt the fear of standing before your Lord—the kind that makes you tremble? If not, are you truly engaging with the Qur'an as revelation, or are you just seeking comfortable experiences that leave your soul unchallenged?

The Divine Wisdom in the Interruption of Revelation
Buti explains the divine wisdom behind the interruption of revelation after the first encounter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the pause in revelation after the first encounter serves as a divine miracle that refutes the theory that revelation is a product of internal meditation.

Core Idea
The pause in revelation proves it was external, not internal.

Buti examines the Prophet's psychological state after the first revelation and the subsequent six-month break. This pause, far from being a sign of doubt, is presented as a powerful miracle that decisively refutes modern materialist explanations of revelation. Before reading the passage, consider how a sudden interruption counters the idea of self-generated inspiration.

Guided Path
1
Enter the narrative of the first revelation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the Prophet's initial fear that the visitor might be from the jinn, and Khadija's reassurance based on his character.
Observe how Buti uses historical details to build his argument.
2
See the external verification through Waraqa
Buti highlights the visit to Waraqa ibn Nawfal, a learned Christian, as confirmation that the revelation matches what previous prophets received.
This step removes confusion by providing an external witness.
3
Analyze the miracle of the pause
Focus on the six-month interruption. Buti argues that this pause is a miracle because it refutes the claim that revelation was an internal psychological illumination.
If revelation were internal, it would not suddenly stop and then resume.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتجلى مزيد من صورة المفاجأة المخيفة لديهم ، في توهمه بأن هذا الذي رآه وغطه وكلمه في الغار قد يكون طائفاً من الجن ، إذ قال لخديجة بعد أن أخبرها الخبر : ( لقد خشيت على نفسي ( أي من الجان . ولكنها طمأنته بأنه ليس ممن يطولهم أذى الشياطين والجان لما فيه من الأخلاق الفاضلة والصفات الحميدة وقد كان الله عز وجل قادراً أن يربط على قلب رسوله ويطمئن نفسه بأن هذا الذي كلمه ليس إلا جبريل : ملك من ملائكة الله جاء ليخبره أنه رسول الله إلى الناس ولكن الحكمة الإلهية الباهرة اقتضت إظهار الانفصال التام بين شخصية محمد قبل البعثة وشخصيته بعدها ، وبيان أن شيئاً من أركان العقيدة الإسلامية أو التشريع الإسلامي لم يطبخ في ذهن الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام سابقاً ولم يتصور الدعوة إلى شيء منه سلفاً ثم إن فيما ألهم الله خديجة من الذهاب به عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى ورقة بن نوفل وعرض الأمر عليه ) وهو الشيخ الهرم العليم بشؤون النصرانية واليهودية ) ، تأكيداً من جانب آخر بأن هذا الذي فوجئ به عليه الصلاة والسلام إنما هو الوحي الإلهي الذي كان قد أنزل على الأنبياء من قبله ، وإزالة لغاشية اللبس التي كانت تحوم حول نفسه بالخوف والتصورات المختلفة عن تفسير مارآه وسمعه • أما انقطاع الوحي بعد ذلك ، وتلبثه ستة أشهر أو أكثر ، على الخلاف المعروف فيه ، فينطوي على مثل المعجزة الإلهية الرائعة . إذ في ذلك أبلغ الرد على ما يفسر به محترفو الغزو الفكري الوحي النبوي ، من أنه الإشراق النفسي المنبعث لديه من طول التأمل والتفكير ، وأنه أمر داخلي منبعث من أعماق ذاته + لقد شاء الله عز وجل أن يحتجب عنه الملك الذي رآه لأول مرة في غار
And further of the frightening surprise is manifested in his imagining that what he saw, covered, and spoke to in the cave might be a visitor from the jinn, for he said to Khadija after telling her the news: 'I fear for myself' (i.e., from the jinn). But she reassured him that he is not among those whom the harm of devils and jinn afflicts, because of the noble morals and praiseworthy qualities he possessed. And God Almighty was able to strengthen the heart of His Messenger and reassure him that the one who spoke to him was none other than Jibril, an angel from God's angels who came to inform him that he is the Messenger of God to people. But the dazzling divine wisdom necessitated showing the complete separation between Muhammad's personality before the mission and his personality after it, and demonstrating that nothing of the pillars of the Islamic creed or Islamic legislation had been cooked in the mind of the Messenger, peace and blessings be upon him, beforehand, nor had he previously imagined calling to any of it. Then, in what God inspired Khadija to take him, peace and blessings be upon him, to Waraqa ibn Nawfal and present the matter to him—and he was the old sage knowledgeable about Christianity and Judaism—there is confirmation from another aspect that what he was surprised by is indeed the divine revelation that had been sent down to the prophets before him, and removal of the veil of confusion that was hovering around his soul due to fear and various perceptions about interpreting what he saw and heard. As for the interruption of revelation after that, and its pause for six months or more, according to the known difference of opinion, it contains a wonderful divine miracle. For in that is the most powerful refutation of what the professionals of intellectual invasion interpret prophetic revelation to be: that it is the psychological illumination emanating from prolonged meditation and thought, and that it is an internal matter emanating from the depths of his self. God Almighty willed to conceal from him the angel whom he saw for the first time in the cave.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage continues the argument by examining the Prophet's state after the first revelation. Buti notes that the Prophet himself feared it might be from the jinn (ṭā'if min al-jinn), as he told Khadija. Khadija reassured him based on his virtuous character. God could have immediately reassured the Prophet, but divine wisdom (ḥikma ilāhiyya) required showing a complete separation (infiṣāl tāmm) between his pre-mission personality and his post-mission personality. This proves that none of the Islamic creed or legislation had been premeditated in his mind. Furthermore, God inspired Khadija to take the Prophet to her cousin Waraqa ibn Nawfal, a learned Christian and Jew, to confirm that this revelation was the same as that given to previous prophets. This external verification removes any confusion. Then Buti highlights the interruption (inqiṭā') of revelation for about six months (or more, according to different reports). This pause is presented as a divine miracle (mu'jiza ilāhiyya) that refutes the claim of intellectual invaders (al-ghazw al-fikrī) that revelation is merely psychological illumination (ishrāq nafsī) from prolonged meditation. If it were internal, it would not suddenly stop and then resume. The concealment of the angel reinforces its external origin.

انقطاع الوحي
معجزة

إشراق نفسي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the interruption of revelation indicates that the Prophet was unsure or that revelation was not continuous.
Correction: Buti argues that the pause was a divine miracle that refutes the idea that revelation is an internal psychological process, and instead confirms its external divine origin.

Checkpoint
Why does Buti consider the interruption of revelation for six months a miracle?
A) Because it shows the Prophet was not in control of the revelation.
B) Because it refutes the claim that revelation is a continuous internal psychological process.
C) Because it allowed the Prophet to rest.
D) Because it proves the revelation came from jinn.

Key Takeaway
The six-month pause in revelation is a divine miracle that proves revelation is external and not a product of the Prophet's own mind.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you felt spiritually abandoned or distant from God? In light of the Prophet's six-month pause, what if that silence is actually a miracle meant to deepen your certainty—not a sign of failure? Will you wait patiently or demand an immediate answer?
?
The Prophet, even in his fear, did not deny what he experienced but sought external confirmation through Khadija and Waraqa. When you face doubt about your faith, do you humbly seek verification from those with knowledge and experience, or do you withdraw into your own thoughts? Which path truly honors the prophetic model?
?
If the revelation had been a product of the Prophet's own mind, it would have been continuous. But it paused. Your own spiritual insights and inspirations—are they from within or from above? How can you tell? Does the existence of sustained periods of silence in your life drive you to seek God more, or to give up?

Objection: Why Was Revelation Not Seen by All?
Buti defends the private nature of revelation against a sensory objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the limitation of human sight and God's creative power provide a rational defense for the private nature of prophetic revelation.

Core Idea
Sight is not the measure of existence; revelation is real even if unseen.

An objector asks why revelation was only witnessed by the Prophet and not his companions. Buti responds by challenging the assumption that visibility proves existence. Our eyes have limited range, and God can enhance vision as He wills. This lesson unpacks the objection and its powerful answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the question being raised and the underlying assumption that revelation should be visible to all.
The objector assumes that if revelation were real, everyone present would see it.
2
Analyze the first part of the answer
Buti's first response: existence is not conditional on being seen. Consider the example of distant objects that exist but cannot be seen. This refutes the idea that unseen means nonexistent.
3
Understand the second part of the answer
Buti adds that God, the Creator of eyes, can increase the power of any eye to see what others cannot. This explains why only the Prophet witnessed revelation.
This highlights God's omnipotence and the special role of the Prophet.
4
Reflect on Malik bin Nabe's illustration
The quote about color blindness and light spectra shows that different eyes perceive differently. This is a practical demonstration that sight is relative.
The example strengthens the argument by appealing to observable science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما عاد بعد ذلك سائل يقول : فلماذا كان ينزل الوحي عليه [لعل الله علاوه؟]، وهو بين الكثير من أصحابه فلا الملك أحد يرى منهم سواه ؟
والجواب أنه ليس من شرط وجود الموجودات أن ترى بالأبصار ، إذ إن وسيلة الإبصار فينا محددة بجد معين ، وإلا لاقتضى ذلك أن يصبح الشيء معدوماً إذا ابتعد عن البصر بعداً يمنع من رؤيته . على أن من اليسير على الله جــل وهو الخالق لهذه العيون المبصرة أن يزيد في قوة ماشاء منها فيرى ما لاتراه العيون الأخرى ، يقول مالك بن نبي في هذا الصدد : جلاله
( إن عمى الألوان مثلاً يقدم لنا حالة نموذجية ، لا يمكن أن ترى فيها بعض الألوان بالنسبة لكل العيون ، وهناك أيضاً مجموعة من الإشعاعات الضوئية دون الضوء الأحمر وفوق الضوء البنفسجي لاتراها أعيننا ، ولاشيء يثبت عملياً أنهـا كذلك بالنسبة لجميع العيون ، فقد توجد عيون يمكن أن تكون أقل أو أكثر حساسية ((1))
(1) الظاهرة القرآنية : ص ۱۲۷ .
And perhaps after that a questioner returns and says: 'Why was the revelation sent down upon him [لعل الله علاوه?] while he was among many of his companions, yet none of the people [or: the angel?] sees him besides them?' The answer is that it is not a condition of the existence of existing things that they be seen by eyes, for the means of sight in us is limited to a specific range, otherwise it would necessitate that a thing become non-existent if it distances from the sight a distance that prevents seeing it. Moreover, it is easy for God—Glory be to Him—who is the Creator of these seeing eyes, to increase the power of any of them so that it sees what other eyes do not see. Malik bin Nabe says in this regard: 'Color blindness, for example, presents us with a typical case, in which some colors cannot be seen by all eyes. There is also a group of light radiations below red light and above violet light that our eyes do not see, and nothing practically proves that they are such with respect to all eyes. For there may exist eyes that could be less or more sensitive.' (1) The Quranic Phenomenon, p. 127.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the reality of revelation, and Buti answers it using the limitation of human sight. The objector asks: why was the revelation only witnessed by the Prophet and not by his companions? Buti replies that existence is not dependent on being seen; our eyes have a limited range. Moreover, God can enhance the vision of whomever He wills. Malik bin Nabe's quote about color blindness and light spectra illustrates that different eyes perceive differently, so it is not necessary for revelation to be observable by all. The passage defends the possibility of private revelation against a sensory-empiricist objection.

الإبصار
الموجودات
محدودية الإبصار

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That revelation must be visible to all to be real or that it is a hallucination because only the Prophet saw it.
Correction: Existence does not require visibility; our sight is limited, and God can grant special perception to His prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of Malik bin Nabe's quote used by Buti?
A) Eyes have limited sensitivity and cannot see all things.
B) Revelation is invisible to everyone.
C) Color blindness is a universal condition.
D) God increases vision only for prophets.

Key Takeaway
The existence of revelation does not depend on universal visibility; our sight is limited and God can grant special perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth of the unseen (like the reality of angels, the torment of the grave, or the scales on the Day of Judgment) simply because you cannot perceive it with your senses? How does this lesson's argument about the limits of sight challenge that tendency? Commit today to recite one verse about the unseen every morning and act as if you see it.
?

How does the lesson's explanation of God granting special vision to the Prophet help you overcome any lingering doubt? Write down a specific doubt you have held and then write the correction from this passage beside it.
?
Reflect on a time you judged something as impossible because your senses could not perceive it—perhaps a miracle, a divine decree, or an attribute of Allah. How does the scientific analogy of invisible light spectra humble your reliance on your own sight? What is one practical change you will make to prioritize revealed knowledge over empirical observation in your daily life?

The Clear Distinction Between Quran and Hadith
Buti presents the first indication: the clear distinction between Quran and Hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's different treatment of Quran and Hadith proves that the Quran is verbatim divine speech.

Core Idea
The Quran is God's exact words; Hadith is God's meaning in the Prophet's words.

How did the Prophet himself distinguish between the Quran and his own sayings? His actions provide a clear answer. This lesson examines his practice of immediately recording the Quran while entrusting Hadith to memory, and the theological reason behind this difference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between Quran and Hadith.
2
Identify the two types of revelation
The passage distinguishes two forms: Quran is revealed with words and letters via Gabriel; Hadith is revealed in meaning but worded by the Prophet. Find the specific phrases that describe each.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does this distinction matter? It shows that the Quran is not the Prophet's own speech, countering the claim that revelation is merely psychological.
This connects to the broader argument against psychoanalysis of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - التمييز الواضح بين القرآن والحديث، إذ كان يأمر بتسجيل الأول فوراً، على حين يكتفي بأن يستودع الثاني ذاكرة أصحابه، لا لأن الحديث كلام من عنده لا علاقة للنبوة به، بل لأن القرآن موحى به إليه بالألفاظ والحروف ذاتها بواسطة جبريل عليه السلام، أما الحديث فمعناه وحي من الله عز وجل، ولكن لفظه وتركيبه من عنده عليه الصلاة والسلام، فكان يحاذر أن يختلط كلام الله عز وجل الذي تلقاه من جبريل بكلامه هو.
1. The clear distinction between the Quran and the Hadith, for he used to command the recording of the former immediately, while he sufficed with entrusting the latter to the memory of his companions, not because the Hadith is speech from himself having no connection to prophethood, but because the Quran was revealed to him with the very words and letters by means of Gabriel (peace be upon him). As for the Hadith, its meaning is revelation from God Almighty, but its wording and composition are from himself (peace and blessings be upon him). Thus he was cautious that the speech of God Almighty which he received from Gabriel should not become mixed with his own speech.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents the first indication that revelation is not a mere psychological phenomenon. The Prophet distinguished between the Quran and his own sayings (Hadith) in a clear manner: he ordered the Quran to be recorded immediately, while Hadith was only entrusted to memory. This distinction shows that the Prophet knew the Quran was verbatim divine speech (lafẓan and ḥarfan) from Gabriel, whereas Hadith is divinely inspired in meaning but expressed in the Prophet's own words. He was careful not to mix the two, proving he was not fabricating the Quran.

الحديث
الوحي
جبريل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That both the Quran and Hadith are equally the literal word of God.
Correction: This passage shows that the Quran is verbatim divine speech, while the Hadith is divinely inspired in meaning but worded by the Prophet.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet order the Quran to be recorded immediately but not the Hadith?
A) The Quran is verbatim divine speech; the Hadith is inspired in meaning only.
B) The Hadith is less important than the Quran.
C) The companions preferred to memorize the Hadith.
D) He feared the Quran would be lost.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's different treatment of Quran and Hadith proves that the Quran is verbatim divine speech, while Hadith is divinely inspired in meaning but expressed in human words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly internalize that you are hearing Allah's exact words—not just a human text? How does that awareness change the way you read, listen, and respond? Commit to pausing before each recitation to remember this reality.
?
The Prophet was extremely cautious not to mix Allah's words with his own. In your daily life, where do you tend to confuse divine commands with your personal desires or cultural norms? What step can you take today to make that distinction clearer in one area?
?
If the meaning of every Hadith is from Allah, how seriously do you take the Prophet's teachings in matters where you struggle to obey? Is there a hadith you have been neglecting or rationalizing away? Resolve to act on one such hadith this week as if Allah Himself were speaking to you through it.

Prophetic Silence and Correction: A Divine Indicator
Buti presents the second indication: prophetic silence and correction by revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's silence and correction by revelation demonstrate that the Quran is divine in origin.

Core Idea
The Prophet's silence and correction show the Quran is divine, not his own.

Buti presents a second powerful indication that the Quran is from Allah: the Prophet's own behavior. Sometimes he remained silent when asked questions, waiting for revelation. Other times, his actions were corrected by Quranic verses, even with gentle reproach. This shows that the Quran was not his personal opinion or invention.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two scenarios described: the Prophet's silence when asked, and his actions being corrected by revelation.
The phrase 'صلىالله' is a garbled text from OCR; ignore it.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Identify the first scenario: the Prophet remains silent on some questions until revelation comes. The second: he takes a course of action, then revelation diverts him from it, sometimes with reproach.
These are distinct but complementary proofs.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: If the Prophet could not answer on his own and could be corrected, then the Quran must be from a source beyond his own mind—divine revelation.
This directly supports the claim that the Quran is not from human authorship.

Commentary
This passage presents the second indication: the Prophet's own practice shows that the Quran is not from his own mind. Sometimes he was asked questions but remained silent until Quranic revelation came, even if a long time passed. This demonstrates that he did not answer from personal opinion. Furthermore, at times he would adopt a certain course of action, only to have Quranic verses reveal a different command, sometimes even with gentle reproach. This shows the Quran was not his own invention but a divine corrective.

Third Indication: Illiteracy and Historical Knowledge
Buti presents the third indication: the Prophet's illiteracy and knowledge of past stories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's illiteracy and his accurate knowledge of past events serve as a decisive proof that the Quran is divine revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's illiteracy proves his historical knowledge came only from Allah.

Buti now presents the third indication: the fact that the Prophet ﷺ was unlettered yet accurately narrated detailed stories of past prophets and nations. This is impossible for a human to know through natural means, especially psychic introspection. The passage shows that such knowledge must be from divine revelation, and the Quran itself points to this as a sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how Buti states the fact of illiteracy and the impossibility of knowing historical facts by psychic means.
The verse at the end reinforces the point.
2
Understand the nature of psychic unveiling
Buti rejects that historical facts can be known through 'mukashafah nafsiyyah' (psychic unveiling). Think about why this is impossible.
3
Connect the verse to the argument
The verse (Yunus 94) tells the Prophet to ask the People of the Book if he doubts. But he had no doubt. This shows the Quran's stories are confirmed by previous scriptures, yet he was unlettered.
The verse reference in the text is Al-Ankabut 48, but it is actually Yunus 94; we keep as given.

This proves that the Quranic stories are divine revelation. The verse quoted (from Yunus, though referenced as Al-Ankabut) directs the Prophet to seek confirmation from the People of the Book if he doubted, but he was certain, further confirming divine origin.

The Fourth Indication: Pre-Prophethood Truthfulness
Buti presents the fourth indication: pre-prophethood truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's long-standing reputation for truthfulness among his people before prophethood serves as a rational indication that his claim to prophethood was genuine.

Core Idea
A forty-year reputation for truthfulness is strong evidence that the Prophet was truthful in his claim.

Buti now presents the fourth indication: the Prophet's pre-prophethood truthfulness. For forty years before receiving revelation, the Prophet (peace be upon him) was known among his people as al-Sadiq al-Amin. This public reputation, Buti argues, necessitates that he was truthful with himself. When he encountered the phenomenon of revelation, he would have examined it honestly and resolved any doubts. The verse from Surah Yunus and the Prophet's response confirm this process.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti uses a logical necessity argument: 40 years of truthfulness with people → truthfulness with self.
2
Identify the logical argument
The passage states that because the Prophet was truthful with his people for 40 years, he must have been truthful with himself. This means he would have honestly studied the revelation and resolved any doubts.
The key phrase is 'يستدعي أن يكون' – 'necessitates that he be'.
3
Examine the Qur'anic verse
The verse from Yunus (94) addresses the possibility of doubt. Buti presents it as commentary on the Prophet's initial reflections. Understand that the verse directs him to ask the People of the Book if in doubt.
The verse is presented as a divine confirmation of the Prophet's investigative process.
4
Reflect on the narrated response
The Prophet's reported response 'I do not doubt and I do not ask' shows that after his honest investigation, he reached absolute certainty. This removes any suggestion that he was deluded.
This response is key to the indication: it shows the truthfulness of his claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إن صدق النبي [لعل الله؟] أربعين سنة مع قومه واشتهاره فيهم بذلك يستدعي أن يكون، من قبل ذلك، صـادقـاً مع نفسه، ولذا فلا بد أن يكون قد قضى في دراسته لظاهرة الوحي على أي شك يخايل لعينيه أو فكره وانظر إلى هذه الآية التي جاءت تعليقاً على تأملاته ودراسته الأولى في محاولة لاستكشاف حقيقة ما قد ساوره من هذا الأمر: ﴿ فَإِنْ كُنْتَ في شَكٍّ مِمَّا أنْزَلْنا إِلَيْكَ فاسْأل الَّذِينَ يَقْرَوُونَ الكِتابَ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ . لَقَدْ جَاءَكَ الحَقُّ مِنْ رَبِّكَ فَلا تَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْمُمْتَرِينَ ﴾ [ يونس : ٩٤ ] . ولذا روي أن النبي [الإ؟] قال بعد نزول هذه الآية لاأشك ولا أسأل .
4. Indeed, the truthfulness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) for forty years with his people and his fame among them for that necessitates that he was, before that, truthful with himself. Therefore, he must have resolved in his study of the phenomenon of revelation any doubt that assailed his eyes or his mind. And look at this verse which came as a commentary on his reflections and his initial study in an attempt to discover the truth of what had troubled him from this matter: 'So if you are in doubt about what We have revealed to you, then ask those who read the Book before you. The truth has come to you from your Lord, so do not be among the doubters.' [Yunus: 94]. Hence it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said after the revelation of this verse: 'I do not doubt and I do not ask.'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth indication: the Prophet's reputation for truthfulness among his people for forty years before prophethood implies that he would naturally be truthful with himself. When he received revelation, he would investigate it honestly and resolve any initial doubts. The verse from Surah Yunus (94) appears to address that process, directing him to ask the People of the Book if he doubted, but the narrated response shows he was certain. This demonstrates that he was not deluded but rather critically examined the revelation and found it true.

Misconception: The Prophet was initially uncertain about the revelation, implying the revelation was not clear.
Correction: The Prophet was not uncertain; he investigated honestly and reached certainty, as shown by his response.

B) He was asked to doubt the revelation.
C) He should not ask the People of the Book.
D) He was already certain and did not need to ask.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's forty-year reputation for truthfulness among his people serves as a strong rational indication that he was truthful in his claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophet's Silence and Divine Correction
Buti enumerates two signs of revelation-based guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's deliberate silence on some questions and occasional divine correction of his actions demonstrate that his guidance came solely from revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's silence was not ignorance—it was waiting for God's word.

This passage offers two powerful observations from the Prophet's life that confirm the divine origin of his message. The first is his practice of remaining silent when asked about matters until the Quranic revelation arrived. The second is that the Quran sometimes corrected his own actions, even with gentle rebuke. These signs show that the Prophet did not speak or act from personal desire, but from revelation alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice the two distinct scenarios Buti describes.
Pay attention to the words 'السكوت' and 'العتب'.
2
Identify the two signs
Find the two main points: (1) the Prophet's silence until revelation came, and (2) the Quran correcting his actions. How does each one prove revelation?
These are separate proofs that together strengthen the argument.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: What would it mean if the Prophet spoke immediately from his own knowledge? Why is waiting for revelation more convincing? How does divine correction show he was not the author of the Quran?
The passage is a proof of prophethood from the nature of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يُسألُ عن بعض الأمور، فلا يجيب عليها، وربما مرَّ على سكوته زمن طويل، حتى إذا نزلت آية من القرآن في شأن ذلك السؤال، طلب السائل وتلا عليه ما نزل من القرآن في شأن سؤاله. وربما تصرف الرسول في بعض الأمور على وجه معين، فتنزل آيات من القرآن تصرفه عن ذلك الوجه: وربما انطوت على عتب عليه أو ملامة له.

And perhaps the Messenger acted in some matters in a specific manner, then verses of the Qur'an would come down turning him away from that manner, and perhaps they included rebuke or blame upon him.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents two signs that the Prophet's guidance came from God, not his own mind. First, when asked about something he did not know, he would not answer immediately but would wait for revelation, sometimes for a long period. When the revelation came, he would then call the questioner and recite the relevant verses. Second, sometimes the Prophet would act in a certain way based on his own judgment, but then revelation would come to correct him, sometimes even containing a gentle rebuke. These observations demonstrate that the Prophet did not invent the message; rather, he submitted to divine guidance even when it redirected his own choices. The passage is a proof of prophethood from the nature of revelation.

The Prophet's Illiteracy as a Proof of Revelation
Buti argues that the Prophet's illiteracy proves the Qur'an's divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's illiteracy is a decisive proof that the Qur'an is divine revelation, not human invention.

Core Idea
The Prophet's illiteracy removes any doubt that he authored the Qur'an himself.

The fact that the Prophet Muhammad was unlettered is often seen as a weakness, but it is actually a powerful sign of his prophethood. In this passage, Ramadan al-Buti explains how the Prophet's inability to read or write rules out the possibility that he could have learned historical accounts from earlier scriptures. This insight, grounded in a Qur'anic verse, turns an apparent limitation into a compelling proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal English translation. Notice how Buti presents the argument concisely.
2
Identify the key claim
Buti argues that the Prophet's illiteracy eliminates the possibility that he obtained historical knowledge from books. Find the sentence that states this.
3
Consider the verse
Buti quotes Qur'an 29:48. Reflect on how this verse directly supports the argument.
The verse explicitly says that if the Prophet had been literate, doubters would have had grounds to doubt.
4
Understand the wisdom
The passage calls this a 'wisdom' (hikma). Think about why illiteracy is not a defect but a divine design.
5
Apply the proof
Summarize the logical chain: illiteracy → no access to books → knowledge must be from God. This is a proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أمياً ... وليس من الممكن أن يعلم إنسان بواسطة المكاشفة النفسية حقائق تاريخية، كقصة يوسف، وأم موسى حينما ألقت وليدها في اليم... وقصة فرعون... ولقد كان هذا من جملة الحكم في كونه أمياً: ﴿ وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُو مِن قَبْلِهِ مِن كِتَابٍ وَلَا تَخُطُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذًا لَّارْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٤٨].
The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) was unlettered... It is not possible for a person, by means of psychic unveiling, to know historical facts such as the story of Joseph, and the mother of Moses when she cast her infant into the sea... and the story of Pharaoh... And this was among the wisdoms in his being unlettered: {And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you inscribe it with your right hand; otherwise the falsifiers would have doubted} [Al-Ankabut: 48].
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides a proof that the Qur'an is not from human invention. The Prophet was known to be unlettered (ummi), meaning he could not read or write. It is impossible for a person to acquire detailed historical knowledge of past nations, such as the stories of Joseph, Moses' mother, and Pharaoh, through mere psychic intuition or self-enlightenment. If the Prophet had been literate, skeptics could claim he had studied previous scriptures. But since he was illiterate, the only explanation is that this knowledge was revealed to him from God. The Qur'anic verse cited (29:48) confirms this: if he had been able to read and write, the doubters would have had grounds to question. Thus, the Prophet's illiteracy is a wisdom and a sign of the truthfulness of his message.

Key Terms
الأمية
المكاشفة النفسية
الحقائق التاريخية
القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that being unlettered is a defect or a sign of ignorance.
Correction: The passage shows that the Prophet's illiteracy is actually a wisdom that eliminates the possibility of human authorship and confirms divine revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Prophet's illiteracy a proof of the truthfulness of revelation?
A) It shows he was simple-minded and could not fabricate stories.
B) It eliminates the possibility that he learned historical facts from books or teachers.
C) It was a common trait among Arabs at the time.
D) It allowed him to focus on worship without distraction.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's illiteracy seals the proof that the Qur'an is from Allah, not from human learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Prophet, despite being unlettered, conveyed the most profound truths, what excuse do you have for not seeking knowledge of the Quran? How will you change your approach to studying the Quran starting today?
?
The verse says 'otherwise the falsifiers would have doubted.' Are there any areas in your heart where you have doubts about the Quran's divine origin? How does this argument from the Prophet's illiteracy challenge or remove those doubts? What will you do to strengthen your certainty?

The Proof from the Prophet's Forty Years of Truthfulness
Buti argues that the Prophet's long-known truthfulness precludes lying about revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's long-established truthfulness supports the authenticity of his prophethood and revelation.

Core Idea
Forty years of truthfulness make lying about revelation impossible.

How can we be certain that Muhammad (peace be upon him) was truly a prophet? One powerful proof lies in his character before prophethood. For forty years, his community knew him as 'al-Amin' – the trustworthy. This lesson examines how this well-known integrity logically supports the truth of his prophetic claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical structure: premise (truthfulness for 40 years) → conclusion (must be truthful with himself and resolve doubt).
2
Understand the logical argument
The passage argues that a person cannot be truthful for decades and then suddenly lie about the most serious matter. The Prophet's known honesty makes it irrational to doubt his claim.
This is not an emotional appeal but a rational inference.
3
Reflect on the verse and narration
Qur'an 10:94 is presented as a comment on the Prophet's initial reflections. The narration shows his complete certainty after revelation. Notice how the verse uses a conditional that is immediately resolved.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Some think the verse implies the Prophet doubted. But the narration clarifies: he said 'I do not doubt, and I do not ask.' The verse was a hypothetical instruction, not an indication of actual doubt.
Understanding this nuance prevents misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إن صدق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أربعين سنة مع قومه واشتهاره فيهم بذلك يستدعي أن يكون، من قبل ذلك، صادقاً مع نفسه، ولذا فلا بد أن يكون قد قضى في دراسته لظاهرة الوحي على أي شك يخالج عينيه أو فكره. وانظر إلى هذه الآية التي جاءت تعليقاً على تأملاته ودراسته الأولى في محاولة لاستكشاف حقيقة ما قد ساوره من هذا الأمر: ﴿ فَإِن كُنتَ فِي شَكٍّ مِّمَّا أَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ فَاسْأَلِ الَّذِينَ يَقْرَءُونَ الْكِتَابَ مِن قَبْلِكَ ۚ لَقَدْ جَاءَكَ الْحَقُّ مِن رَّبِّكَ فَلَا تَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْمُمْتَرِينَ ﴾ [يونس: ٩٤]. ولذا روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال بعد نزول هذه الآية: لا أشك ولا أسأل.
4. Indeed, the truthfulness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) for forty years among his people and his fame among them for that requires that he be, before that, truthful with himself. Therefore, he must have resolved in his study of the phenomenon of revelation any doubt that might assail his eyes or his mind. And look at this verse which came as a comment on his reflections and his initial study in an attempt to discover the truth of what had preoccupied him about this matter: {So if you are in doubt about what We have revealed to you, then ask those who read the Book before you. The truth has certainly come to you from your Lord, so never be among the doubters} [Yunus: 94]. Hence it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said after this verse was revealed: 'I do not doubt, and I do not ask.'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof for prophethood. The Prophet was known among his people for forty years as a truthful and trustworthy person ('al-Amin'). Such a well-established character cannot suddenly become a liar, especially regarding the most serious claim of prophethood. Therefore, the Prophet must have been truthful with himself when he experienced revelation; he would have thoroughly examined it and resolved any doubt. The Qur'anic verse (10:94) is cited to show that even the Prophet, in the early stages, was commanded to consult the People of the Book if he had any doubt – and the response indicates that the truth had already arrived. The narration that the Prophet said 'I do not doubt, and I do not ask' after the verse shows that his certainty was complete. Thus, the long record of truthfulness supports the authenticity of revelation.

Key Terms
الصدق
الشك
اليقين
الكتابيون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse (10:94) implies the Prophet actually doubted the revelation.
Correction: The verse is a conditional statement. The Prophet's response ('I do not doubt, and I do not ask') shows he had no doubt. The instruction to ask was hypothetical, intended to affirm the truth.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument in this passage about the Prophet's truthfulness?
A) He was truthful only after receiving revelation.
B) His forty-year reputation for truthfulness makes it impossible for him to lie about revelation.
C) He was truthful because he feared his people's reaction.
D) The verse shows he doubted until he asked the People of the Book.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's forty-year record of truthfulness is a rational proof that he could not have lied about receiving revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was truthful with himself even about the most extraordinary claim. When have you been dishonest with yourself about a spiritual matter? Will you commit today to truthfulness with yourself, even if it is uncomfortable?
?
The Prophet's forty-year reputation made his words weighty. If your life were examined, would your words and actions align enough to make others trust your claims about God? What change do you need to make starting now?
?
The Prophet said 'I do not doubt and I do not ask.' Is there an area of your faith where you entertain unnecessary doubts instead of seeking certainty? What step will you take this week to move from doubt to conviction?

Proof that Revelation is from God via Reductio ad Absurdum
Buti proves divine origin of revelation by reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses reductio ad absurdum to prove that revelation comes from God, by showing that alternative explanations lead to absurd consequences.

Core Idea
If revelation were human invention, it would contradict the Prophet's character and experience – an absurdity.

Buti has already established that revelation is a real phenomenon. Now he considers what it could be: is it divine, or could it be mere inspiration, poetry, or mental illness? He employs a logical technique called reductio ad absurdum: assume the negation, derive an impossibility, and thus prove the original claim. This passage walks through that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
We have already affirmed that revelation events occurred. Now we need to explain their source.
This argument builds on prior acceptance of the reality of revelation.
2
Consider the deniers' hypothesis
Buti asks: what if revelation is what the deniers claim – mere inspiration or poetry?
This is the hypothesis to be tested.
3
Derive absurd consequences
Poets and inspired ones do not experience physical tremors. Also, the Prophet cannot combine perfect honesty with deception. These consequences are absurd.
The absurdities are both empirical (lack of physical signs) and logical (incompatible character traits).
4
Conclude the only viable explanation
Since the hypothesis leads to absurdity, it must be false. The remaining truth is that revelation is from an external divine source.
The argument also previews that the Quran itself confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان لابد من التصديق بذلك بعد أن صدقناه في إثبات أصل الوحي . ولما فرضنا ( مع تصديق هذه الوقائع واعتمادها ( أن يكون الوحي شيئاً مما يقوله الجاحدون بنبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وجدنا هذه الفرضية تستلزم لزوماً بينـاً نتائج باطلة لا يقبلها عقل أي مفكر . فالملهمون والشعراء لا يقعون فريسة لارتعاد الفرائص واصفرار اللون عندما يمارسون شيئاً من التفكير ، ومحمد الله لا يعقل أن يكون منطوياً في وقت واحد على أدق صفات الأمانة والصدق وعلى أحط مظاهر التدجيل والكذب والتمثيل . وإذا ظهر بطلان هذه النتائج في ميزان أي عقل ، ظهر بطلان الفرضية التي استلزمتها . وإذا بطلت تلك الفرضيات . ثبت مادلت عليه وقائع النصوص نفسها من أن الوحي لم يكن إلا تلقياً منه عليه الصلاة والسلام الحقيقة خارجة عن كيانه بعيدة عن إرادته ، لم يكن مستشرفاً لها ولا متوقعاً شيئاً منها ، وسنجد بعـد ذلك عندما نتحدث عن القرآن وظاهرته أنه ليس إلا جبريل جاءه برسالة إلى البشر من عند الله
So it was necessary to affirm that after we affirmed the establishment of the origin of revelation. And when we hypothesized (while affirming these facts and relying on them) that revelation was something of what the deniers of his prophethood (peace and blessings be upon him) say, we found that this hypothesis necessarily entails clearly absurd results that no intellect of any thinker would accept. For the inspired ones and poets do not fall prey to trembling of the limbs and yellowing of the face when they engage in some thinking, and Muhammad (peace be upon him) cannot reasonably combine at one time the most precise qualities of trustworthiness and truthfulness with the lowest forms of deception, lying, and pretense. And if the falsehood of these results appears in the balance of any intellect, then the falsehood of the hypothesis that entailed them appears. And if those hypotheses are false, then what is indicated by the facts of the texts themselves is established: that revelation was nothing but a reception from him (peace and blessings be upon him) of a reality external to his being, far from his will; he was not anticipating it nor expecting anything from it. And we will find later, when we talk about the Quran and its phenomenon, that it is only Gabriel who came to him with a message to humanity from God.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (burhan) for the divine origin of revelation, using reductio ad absurdum. The author begins by stating that after affirming the reality of revelation itself, one must consider the alternative hypotheses proposed by those who deny prophethood. He then posits a hypothesis: that revelation is like what the deniers claim—perhaps from poetic inspiration or mental imagination. He then shows that this hypothesis entails absurd consequences. Specifically, the inspired ones and poets do not experience physical tremors and pallor when thinking, yet the Prophet did. Moreover, the Prophet possessed the highest qualities of trustworthiness and truthfulness, which are incompatible with deception and lying. Since these consequences are absurd to any rational mind, the hypothesis that revelation is human fabrication must be false. Consequently, the only remaining truth is that revelation is an external reality received by the Prophet, independent of his own will or expectation. The author concludes by previewing a later discussion on the Quran, affirming it is from Gabriel.

Key Terms
الوحي (revelation)
الفرضية (hypothesis)
النتائج الباطلة (absurd conclusions)
الملهمون (the inspired ones)
الشعراء (poets)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument that revelation is from God is based on blind faith or circular reasoning.
Correction: Buti does not begin by assuming revelation is divine; he objectively examines the possibilities and eliminates those that lead to absurdities, leaving only the divine hypothesis standing.

Checkpoint
What method does Buti use to prove that revelation is from God?
A) Direct quotation from the Quran
B) Reductio ad absurdum by showing alternative hypotheses lead to absurdities
C) Appeal to the Prophet's miracles
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Buti's reductio ad absurdum shows that the only rational explanation for the Prophet's revelations is that they came from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were asked to defend the divine origin of the Quran using Buti's argument, could you do it without hesitation? Or do you rely on blind acceptance? What would it take for you to own this proof personally?
?
The Prophet's physical reaction of trembling shows that revelation was not a comfortable, humanly-controlled experience. Have you ever treated divine guidance as something convenient or comfortable? How does this passage challenge your assumptions about what it means to receive truth from God?
?
Buti argues that the Prophet cannot simultaneously be truthful and deceptive. Think of a time when you claimed to follow the Prophet but acted inconsistently with his truthfulness. What would it cost you to align your life fully with the integrity that the Prophet embodied?

Adam and Muhammad: The First and Last Prophets
Buti links belief in revelation to belief in prophets, specifying Adam as first and Muhammad as last.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in revelation logically leads to belief in Muhammad's prophethood, and that Adam is the first prophet and Muhammad the last.

Core Idea
Belief in revelation demands belief in Muhammad, the final prophet.

Having established the reality of revelation, Buti now shows what that means for our belief in prophets. If revelation is real, then Muhammad is a prophet, and from the Quran we learn that Adam was the first prophet and Muhammad the last. This lesson clarifies these two foundational truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Notice the logical flow from revelation to Muhammad to the two points.
Pay attention to the verse from Surat al-Ahzab.
2
Identify the logical sequence
Buti argues: if you are certain of revelation, then you must believe in Muhammad's prophethood, which means believing the Quran is from God. From the Quran, you learn two things: Adam is first prophet, Muhammad is last.
This shows how the previous topic (revelation) connects to prophethood.
3
Reflect on the evidence
For Adam, Buti references the Quranic stories of his creation and descent. For Muhammad, he cites the explicit verse calling him the 'Seal of the Prophets'.
Think about why this evidence is considered clear and decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا
الأنبياء الذين بعثهم الله عزوجل
وكيفية الإيمان بهم

إذا أيقنت أن محمداً الله قد أوحي إليه ، وأيقنت معنى الوحي بالبرهان العلمي القطعي الذي أوضحناه ، كان لا بد أن توقن بنبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وذلك يعني أن تؤمن بأن القرآن كلام الله عز وجل أوحي به إلى رسول الله

فإذا آمنت بالقرآن أنه كلام الله عز وجل ( وسيأتي مزيد من البحث عن القرآن وإعجازه وبرهان أنه من عند الله عز وجل ( اقتضاك ذلك أن تعرف الأمور التالية ، بصدد الإيمان بالرسل والأنبياء

۱ - إن أول نبي أرسله الله تعالى مؤيداً بالوحي والأحكام هو : آدم أبو البشر عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وآخر الأنبياء وهو محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا نبي بعده . فأما نبوة آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام فهي ثابتة بصريح ما أخبرنا الله تعالى من قصة خلقه ثم إنزاله إلى الأرض وتكليفه بالهدى الذي سيأتيه من قبله له ولذريته ( اقرأ قصة آدم في سورة البقرة والأعراف والكهف وطـه ( وأما أن محمداً هو خاتم الأنبياء ، فقد ثبت ذلك بالنصوص الواضحة الصريحة في كتاب الله عز وجل وفي السنة المطهرة . فمن نصوص الكتاب قوله جل جلاله : ما كانَ مُحَمَّدٌ أَبا أَحَدٍ مِنْ رجالِكُمْ وَلكِنْ رَسول الله وخاتَمَ النَّبيِّينَ ، وَكانَ اللهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيماً ) [ الأحزاب : ٤٠ ]
Secondly
The prophets whom God Almighty sent
And how to believe in them

If you are certain that Muhammad (peace be upon him) has been inspired, and you are certain of the meaning of revelation with the decisive scientific proof that we have explained, then it is necessary that you be certain of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), and that means that you believe that the Quran is the speech of God Almighty revealed to the Messenger of God.

So if you believe in the Quran that it is the speech of God Almighty (and further research will come about the Quran and its inimitability and proof that it is from God Almighty), then that requires you to know the following matters regarding belief in the messengers and prophets:

1. The first prophet sent by God Almighty supported by revelation and rulings is: Adam, the father of humanity (peace be upon him), and the last of the prophets is Muhammad (peace be upon him); there is no prophet after him. As for the prophethood of Adam (peace be upon him), it is established by the clear text of what God Almighty has told us of the story of his creation, then his descent to earth, and his obligation with the guidance that would come from Him to him and his progeny (read the story of Adam in Surat al-Baqarah, al-A'raf, al-Kahf, and Ta-Ha). And as for that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets, that has been established by clear and explicit texts in the Book of God Almighty and in the purified Sunnah. Among the texts of the Book is His saying, Exalted is His Majesty: 'Muhammad is not the father of any of your men, but he is the Messenger of God and the Seal of the Prophets; and God is ever of all things Knowing.' [al-Ahzab: 40]
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on the necessity of believing in the prophets after establishing belief in revelation. The author begins by linking belief in Muhammad's prophethood to the prior belief in revelation: if one is certain that revelation has occurred and understands its reality, then one must accept Muhammad as a prophet. This logically entails believing that the Quran is God's speech revealed to him. Then, after a brief preview of a later discussion on the Quran, the author enumerates two essential points regarding belief in the prophets. First, the first prophet is Adam, supported by revelation and rulings, as the Quran recounts his creation and mission. Second, the last prophet is Muhammad, and there is no prophet after him. The author provides scriptural evidence for both: for Adam, the Quranic stories; for Muhammad, the clear verse from Surat al-Ahzab (33:40) that explicitly calls him the 'Seal of the Prophets'. The passage emphasizes that these truths are established by clear texts from the Quran and Sunnah.

الوحي
آدم
خاتم النبيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Muhammad was the first prophet or that there are prophets after him.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Adam was the first prophet and Muhammad is the last; no prophet comes after Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Belief in revelation requires belief in Muhammad as the final prophet, and the Quran confirms Adam as the first prophet.

The Finality of Muhammad's Prophethood: First and Last Prophet
The author enumerates the first and last prophets and provides evidence for finality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural basis for believing that Muhammad is the final prophet, and how the second coming of Jesus does not contradict this.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the seal of the prophets; no new prophet or law after him.

This passage builds on the certainty of revelation to establish the foundational belief in Muhammad as the last prophet. The author provides clear evidence from the Quran and hadith, and addresses a common confusion about Jesus's return. By the end, the learner will appreciate why this doctrine is self-evident for a Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Realize that accepting Muhammad's prophethood is necessary after accepting revelation. The author states that if you are certain of revelation to Muhammad, you must be certain of his prophethood.
This connects belief in revelation to belief in prophethood.
2
Identify the first and last prophet
The passage explicitly states that the first prophet is Adam and the last is Muhammad. Note the Quranic basis for Adam's prophethood and the explicit statement for Muhammad.
This is the core doctrinal point.
3
Examine the proofs for finality
The author cites Quran 33:40 ('Muhammad is not the father of any of your men... Seal of the Prophets') and the hadith of the brick (muttafaq 'alayh). Read these texts carefully.
These are the primary scriptural proofs.
4
Resolve the objection about Jesus
Understand that Jesus's return does not make him a prophet after Muhammad. He comes as a follower implementing Muhammad's law, not as a prophet with a new revelation.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً الأنبياء الذين بعثهم الله عزوجل وكيفية الإيمان بهم إذا أيقنت أن محمداً الله قد أوحي إليه ، وأيقنت معنى الوحي بالبرهان العلمي القطعي الذي أوضحناه ، كان لا بد أن توقن بنبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وذلك يعني أن تؤمن بأن القرآن كلام الله عز وجل أوحي به إلى رسول الله الله فإذا آمنت بالقرآن أنه كلام الله عز وجل ( وسيأتي مزيد من البحث عن القرآن وإعجازه وبرهان أنه من عند الله عز وجل ( اقتضاك ذلك أن تعرف الأمور التالية ، بصدد الإيمان بالرسل والأنبياء ۱ - إن أول نبي أرسله الله تعالى مؤيداً بالوحي والأحكام هو : آدم أبو البشر عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وآخر الأنبياء وهو محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام فلا نبي بعده . فأما نبوة آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام فهي ثابتة بصريح ما أخبرنا الله تعالى من قصة خلقه ثم إنزاله إلى الأرض وتكليفه بالهدى الذي سيأتيه من قبله له ولذريته ( اقرأ قصة آدم في سورة البقرة والأعراف والكهف وطه ( وأما أن محمداً هو خاتم الأنبياء ، فقد ثبت ذلك بالنصوص الواضحة الصريحة في كتاب الله عز وجل وفي السنة المطهرة . فمن نصوص الكتاب قوله جل جلاله : ما كانَ مُحَمَّدٌ أَبا أَحَدٍ مِنْ رجالِكُمْ وَلكِنْ رَسول الله وخاتَمَ النَّبيِّينَ ، وَكانَ اللهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيماً ) [ الأحزاب : ٤٠ ] . ومن نصوص السنة قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الحديث المتفق عليه : مثلي ومثل الأنبياء من قبلي ، كمثل رجل بني بيتـاً فـأحسـنـه وأجملـه إلا موضع لبنة من زاوية ، فجعل الناس يطوفون به ويعجبون له ويقولون : هلاً وضعت هذه اللبنة ؟ فأنا اللبنة وأنا خاتم النبيين » . وهذا من البديهيات التي لا بد من الاعتقاد بها لبناء معنى الإيمان والإسلام في القلب ولا يخالف هذه الحقيقة ما هو ثابت بالأدلة من نزول عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام قرب قيام الساعة ) وسنتحدث عن ذلك في قسم الغيبيات إن شاء الله ) ، فليس معنى ذلك أنه يأتي مؤيداً بوحي وشرع جديد من عند الله عز وجل وإنمـا يأتي منفذاً ومقرراً شريعة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام . أي فليس مجيئه بوصف أنه نبي ينسخ نبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام . ولكنه يأتي مؤكداً ومقرراً لها ، ومنفذاً لشريعته .
Secondly: The prophets whom Allah the Mighty and Majestic sent, and how to believe in them. If you are certain that Muhammad (Allah) received revelation, and you are certain of the meaning of revelation by the definitive scientific proof that we have explained, then it is necessary that you be certain of the prophethood of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. That means that you believe that the Quran is the speech of Allah the Mighty and Majestic, revealed to the Messenger of Allah (Allah). If you believe in the Quran that it is the speech of Allah the Mighty and Majestic (and further research on the Quran, its inimitability, and the proof that it is from Allah the Mighty and Majestic will come later), then that requires you to know the following matters regarding belief in the messengers and prophets: 1. The first prophet sent by Allah the Exalted, supported by revelation and rulings, is Adam, the father of mankind, peace and blessings be upon him. And the last of the prophets is Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him; there is no prophet after him. As for the prophethood of Adam, peace be upon him, it is established by the explicit information that Allah the Exalted has given us of the story of his creation, then his descent to the earth, and his obligation with the guidance that would come to him and his descendants. (Read the story of Adam in Surat al-Baqarah, al-A'raf, al-Kahf, and Taha). As for Muhammad being the seal of the prophets, that has been established by clear and explicit texts in the Book of Allah the Mighty and Majestic and in the purified Sunnah. Among the texts of the Book is His saying, Exalted is His Majesty: "Muhammad is not the father of any of your men, but he is the Messenger of Allah and the Seal of the Prophets, and Allah is of all things Knowing" [al-Ahzab: 40]. Among the texts of the Sunnah is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, in the unanimously agreed-upon hadith: "My example and the example of the prophets before me is like a man who built a house and perfected it and beautified it, except for a place of a brick in a corner. So the people began to go around it and marvel at it and say: 'Why was this brick not placed?' So I am the brick, and I am the seal of the prophets." And this is among the self-evident matters that must be believed in to build the meaning of faith and Islam in the heart. And this fact is not contradicted by what is established by evidence of the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, near the Hour of Resurrection (and we will speak about that in the section on the unseen, if Allah wills). For that does not mean that he comes supported by a new revelation and law from Allah the Mighty and Majestic; rather, he comes as an implementer and affirmers of the law of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. That is, his coming is not in the capacity of a prophet who abrogates the prophethood of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. Rather, he comes affirming and confirming it, and implementing his law.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the necessity of belief in the prophets, specifically focusing on the first and last prophets. The author begins by stating that once one accepts the reality of revelation to Muhammad, one must accept his prophethood and the Quran as divine speech. Then he lists the first required knowledge: the first prophet is Adam and the last is Muhammad. He provides evidence for both: for Adam, from Quranic stories; for Muhammad, from the Quran (33:40) and the hadith of the brick (muttafaq 'alayhi). The author emphasizes that this is a self-evident matter foundational to faith. Then he addresses a potential objection: the second coming of Jesus does not contradict Muhammad's finality because Jesus will come not as a prophet with a new law, but as a follower implementing Muhammad's law. This clarifies that the seal of prophets is not broken by Jesus' return.

Key Terms
نبوة
خاتم النبيين
وحي
الرسول
عيسى عليه السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Jesus' second coming means he is a prophet after Muhammad and brings a new law.
Correction: Jesus comes as a follower of Muhammad's law, not as a prophet with a new revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets?
A) A verse from the Quran and a hadith
B) The story of Adam
C) The descent of Jesus
D) The scientific proof of revelation

Key Takeaway
Muhammad is the final prophet, and no prophet, including Jesus upon his return, will bring a new law.

The Twenty-Five Prophets and Modes of Belief
Listing of twenty-five prophets and the obligation of belief in detail and general.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between believing in prophets in detail (tafsilan) and in general (ijmalan), and you will know the twenty-five prophets named in the Quran.

Core Idea
Belief in prophets has two modes: detailed for the named, general for the unknown.

This passage from a classical aqeedah text clarifies a key aspect of Islamic belief in prophets. The author lists the twenty-five prophets specifically mentioned in the Quran and explains that every Muslim must know and affirm each of them individually. At the same time, we must believe in all other prophets sent by Allah, even though we do not know their names.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses the terms 'تفصيلاً' (in detail) and 'إجمالاً' (in general).
2
Identify the two categories of belief
The passage presents two categories: belief in the named prophets in detail, and belief in other prophets in general. Find where each is mentioned and note the obligation associated.
3
Review the list of 25 prophets
Read through the list of names. See if you are familiar with all of them. This is a key part of Islamic knowledge.
There are slight OCR errors in some names; refer to the corrected list in the commentary.
4
Reflect on the obligation
Consider why it is obligatory to know these 25 individually but only to believe in others generally. How does this affect a Muslim’s everyday practice?
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and complete the activity to solidify the concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲ - ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه أسماء خمسة وعشرين نبياً مرسلاً ، فهؤلاء يجب الاعتقاد بنبوتهم تفصيلاً تفصيلاً ، ومعنى ، ومعنى ذلك أنه لا يجوز للمسلم ( إذا ما سئل عن واحد من هؤلاء الذين نص القرآن على نبوتهم ( أن يجهله أو يجهل كونه نبياً . وهم : آدم ، إدريس ، نوح ، هود ، صالح ، إبراهيم ، لوط ، إسماعيل ، إسحاق ، يعقوب ، يوسف ، شعيب ، أيوب ، ذو الكفل ، موسی ، هارون ، سلیمان ، داود ، إلياس ، اليسع ، يونس ، زكريا ، يحيي ، عيسى ، محمد عليه وعليهم الصلاة والسلام . وهنالك أنبياء آخرون لم يتعرض القرآن لذكرهم تفصيلاً ولم يقص علينا شيئاً من أخبارهم ولكن أخبرنا عنهم في الجملة . فيجب الإيمان بهم أيضاً في الجملة ، أي أن نوقن بأن الله عز وجل أرسل رسلاً وأنبياء كثيرين إلى كل أمة وجماعة ، وفي مختلف الأمكنة والعصور .
2. Allah the Exalted mentioned in His Book the names of twenty-five sent prophets. So it is obligatory to believe in their prophethood in detail. And its meaning is that it is not permissible for a Muslim, if asked about one of these whose prophethood the Quran explicitly states, to be ignorant of him or to be ignorant that he is a prophet. They are: Adam, Idris, Noah, Hud, Salih, Ibrahim, Lut, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, Shu'ayb, Ayyub, Dhul-Kifl, Musa, Harun, Sulayman, Dawud, Ilyas, al-Yasa', Yunus, Zakariyya, Yahya, 'Isa, Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon them. So it is obligatory to believe in them also in general, that we are certain that Allah the Mighty and Majestic sent many messengers and prophets to every nation and group, in different places and times.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the prophets regarding how belief in them is required. The author states that Allah has named twenty-five prophets in the Quran; belief in these prophets is obligatory in detail (tafsilan), meaning one must know each by name and acknowledge their prophethood. He then lists them in order. They include the well-known prophets from Adam to Muhammad. After listing them, the author mentions that there are other prophets not mentioned by name in the Quran, but the Quran speaks of them in general. Belief in these is obligatory in general (ijmalan), meaning we believe that Allah sent many prophets to every nation throughout history, though we do not know their individual identities. The text emphasizes the importance of knowing the named prophets and not being ignorant of them.

Hadith of the Brick: Seal of Prophethood
Buti cites the hadith of the brick to establish the sealing of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the brick establishes Muhammad as the seal of prophets and why this belief is necessary for faith.

Core Idea
The hadith of the brick: prophethood's building is only complete with Muhammad.

Buti presents a key prophetic hadith that uses a vivid analogy to demonstrate the finality of prophethood. This hadith is not just a story but a foundational proof from the Sunna. In this lesson, we will examine the hadith and its implications for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic hadith carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the simile of the house and the missing brick.
This hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh) by Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Understand the analogy
Reflect on the analogy: the beautiful house represents the line of prophets; the missing brick is the place of Muhammad. The people's wonder shows the need for completion.
The brick is placed in a corner, symbolizing a small but essential part.
3
Grasp the author's conclusion
Buti states this hadith is among the self-evident truths (badihiyyat) necessary for building faith and Islam in the heart. Accepting Muhammad as the seal is integral to faith.
This connects the hadith to broader aqeedah foundations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن نصوص السنة قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الحديث المتفق عليه : مثلي ومثل الأنبياء من قبلي ، كمثل رجل بني بيتـاً فـأحسـنـه وأجملـه إلا موضع لبنة من زاوية ، فجعل الناس يطوفون به ويعجبون له ويقولون : هلاً وضعت هذه اللبنة ؟ فأنا اللبنة وأنا خاتم النبيين » . وهذا من البديهيات التي لا بد من الاعتقاد بها لبناء معنى الإيمان والإسلام في القلب

So I am that brick and I am the seal of the prophets.' This is among the self-evident things that must be believed for building the meaning of faith and submission in the heart.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage provides a proof from the Sunna for the finality of prophethood. The hadith uses a simile: the previous prophets are like a beautiful house missing one brick; Muhammad is that brick, completing the building. The author then states that this is a self-evident truth (min al-badihiyyat) necessary for building the structure of faith and Islam in the heart. Accepting Muhammad as the seal is not optional but integral to faith.

Jesus's Descent and the Seal of Prophethood
Buti refutes a potential objection regarding Jesus's descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Jesus's future descent does not contradict the finality of Muhammad's prophethood and how it actually confirms his sharia.

Core Idea
Jesus returns as a follower of Muhammad, not as a prophet with a new law.

One might wonder: if Muhammad is the last prophet, how can Jesus return? This question arises from a misunderstanding. Buti clarifies that Jesus will descend not to bring new revelation but to implement and confirm the sharia of Muhammad. This lesson explores that distinction and affirms the seal of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Buti addresses a potential objection about Jesus's descent.
The passage is a direct response to a common question.
2
Identify the objection and the answer

Look for the contrast between 'ليس معنى ذلك' and 'إنما'.
3
Understand the role of Jesus as implementer
Buti explicitly says Jesus comes to implement and confirm Muhammad's sharia, not as a prophet abrogating it. Reflect on why this preserves the finality of prophethood.
This reinforces that prophethood is sealed; even a prophet returning operates under Muhammad's law.

His coming does not abrogate or contradict the finality of Muhammad's prophethood. The author also mentions that this topic will be treated in detail later in the section on the Unseen.

In this passage, Buti lists the 25 prophets whose names appear explicitly in the Quran.
