This passage is a rhetorical argument presenting the divine plan to abrogate the custom of adoption. The author begins by stating the problem: a deep-rooted custom must be eradicated so that no trace of it remains. The question is posed: what method can achieve this permanent abrogation? The answer is the divinely ordained plan: disturb Zayd's marital life so that he divorces Zaynab, then inspire the Prophet to be ready to marry her, and finally reveal a clear Qur'anic verse commanding the marriage. The story spreads, and the verse becomes widely known, thus establishing the new ruling and erasing the custom. The author then challenges any critic to suggest a better method for abolishing such an entrenched custom, concluding that no rational person could object to this divinely guided plan.

The Story of Zayd and Zaynab
Buti narrates the incident of Zayd and Zaynab up to the Prophet's inner reaction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the incident of Zayd and Zaynab as presented in Islamic sources, including the Prophet's advice and his momentary heart inclination.

Core Idea
The Prophet's advice to Zayd shows his moral excellence despite personal inclination.

This lesson presents the historical incident that later became a point of controversy. Understanding the event as described by Buti is crucial to grasping the theological defense he offers. We will read the passage where Zayd complains about his wife and the Prophet advises him, followed by the Prophet's own inner reaction.

Guided Path
1
Read the incident
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the sequence: Zayd's complaints, the Prophet's repeated advice, and the moment the Prophet sees Zaynab.
The text has some OCR issues, but the meaning is clear.
2
Identify the key actions
List the actions of Zayd (complaining, seeking divorce) and the Prophet (advising, turning away, saying 'Glory be to Allah').
3
Reflect on the Prophet's inner state
Notice that the Prophet's heart moved but he turned away and made a supplication. This sets up the later defense.
The Prophet's reaction shows his mindfulness of Allah.

وهذا ماحدث : فقد تعكر صفو العيش بينهما . وكان زيد يشكو منها غلظة القول وعصيان الأمر والأذى باللسان والتعظم بالشرف ، وأقبل مراراً يستأذن رسول الله في طلاقها ، فيقول له عليه الصلاة والسلام في كل مرة : أمسك عليك زوجك واتق الله . وربما أبصرها خلال هذه المدة ، ذات يوم ، فتحرك قلبه نحوها ، فأشاح بوجهه قائلاً بينه وبين نفسه : « سبحان الله مقلب القلوب فقد ذكرت روايات شيئاً من هذا القبيل، ولست أدري ماهو هذا الذي يدعو إلى التحرج من قبول هذه الرواية أو استشكالها أو الوقوف عندها ) . ماذا من (۱) نقول هذا الكلام لمن رأى أن يتمسك بهذه الرواية التي أشرنا إليها ، ويعدها رواية صحيحة ، اتباعاً لما رواه الطبري والنيسابوري وذكره البيضاوي وابن الجوزي لنوضح له أنها - على فرض أنها صحيحة - لا تصلح معتمداً لبث أي نقيصة في جانب رسول الله وقد ضعفها جمع كبير من علماء الحديث وأئمة التفسير ، ومنهم القرطبي وابن كثير ، قالوا : والرواية الصحيحة المعتمدة في ذلك ما روي عن علي بن الحسين أن النبي كان قد أوحى = هي الشبهة أو الإشكال في أن يريد الله أن يزوج رسوله من مطلقة متبناه لحكمة تشريعية معينة ، فيهيء لذلك سبيله الإنساني المعروف ؟! بل دعني أقول لـك ماذا في أن يتحرك قلب رسول الله الله بالميل إليها ؟ ومتى كان ميل القلوب فعلاً يتعلق به حكم من أحكام الشريعة وقد علمت الدنيـا بـأسـرهـا أن الميل القلبي الأفعال الكسبية والاختيارية ؟ على أني أذكر الانفعالات القسرية وليس من من مرة أخرى أن رسول الله لا و كان قد رآها قبل أن يزوجها من زيد ، ولو أن المسألة كانت مسألة طمع فيها لما منعه أي مانع من أن يتزوج هو منها دون أن بضع بينه وبين هذا الزواج عقبة كأداء من الأعراف الجاهلية . فلما طلقها زيد بعد أن نفذ صبره على احتمال ماكان يلقى منها ، نزل الوحي على رسول الله بهذه الآية صلى الله عليه وسلم : الله إليه أن زيداً يطلق زينب وأنه يتزوجها بتزويج الله إياها . فلما تشكى زيد للنبي خلق زينب وأنها لا تطيعه وأعلمه أنه يريد طلاقها ، قال له على جهة الأدب والوصية : « اتق الله في قولك وأمسك عليك زوجك » وهو يعلم أنه سيفارقها ويتزوجها ، فهذا هو الذي أخفاه في نفسه وعاتبه عليه الباري جل جلاله ، بقوله وتخفي في نفسك ما الله مبديه . ونحن ، فقد آثرنا أن لا نضرب صفحاً عن الرواية الأخرى التي ساقها الطبري وآخرون ، كما يرى البعض ، بل أحببنا أن نكشف عن عصمة سيدنا رسول الله عما يرميـه بـه طائفة من المستشرقين وأرباب الغزو الفكري ، حتى على فرض صحتها ، فهي لا تزيده - على كل حال - إلا رفعة في الخلق وسموا في الجانب . ولا مسوغ لبيان عصمة النبي على أساس تجاهل هذه الرواية أو القطع ببطلانها ، فأنت بذلك تشعر السائل أن الطبري ومن جرى مجراه ممن لم يضعف هذه الرواية لم يبالوا أن يلحقوا النقيصة بخلقه عليه الصلاة والسلام . وحاشاهم عن ذلك . بل إن شأنه أن يزيد في شكوك أصحاب الوساوس وضعاف الإيمان . أولئك الذين لا يعدمون وسيلة من يطلعون منها على هذه الرواية في مصادر قد لا تضعفها ولا تتحدث عن بطلانها . فيمضي أحدهم يلحق النقيصة برسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام زاعماً أنه يسير في ذلك على مذهب الطبري وأمثاله ..!!! أو زاعماً - بخبث - أنه يلحق النقيصة برسول الله على احتمال ضعيف ..!! ومن أخطر آفات هذا التجاهل أنه يقتلع الثقة بالداعية من نفوس هؤلاء الناس ، إنه يجعلهم يتصورون أن أمر هذا الدين بيد « مشايخه » فإذا أعجبهم شيء منه دعموا الأحاديث الواردة فيه وإذا لم يعجبهم أغلقوا طريق النقاش فيه بالتضعيف أو الإنكار أو ادعاء الوضع ( - ۲۱۱ -
And this is what happened: the tranquility of life between them was disturbed. Zayd complained to him of her harsh speech, disobedience of command, verbal harm, and boasting of lineage, and he repeatedly asked the Messenger of Allah for permission to divorce her. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said to him each time: 'Keep your wife and fear Allah.' And perhaps he saw her during this period, one day, and his heart moved towards her, so he turned his face away, saying to himself: 'Glory be to Allah, the Turner of Hearts...' Narrations have mentioned something of this sort, and I do not know what it is that calls for reluctance to accept this narration or to find it problematic or to pause at it. What is (1) we say this to one who sees fit to cling to this narration we have indicated, and considers it a sound narration, following what was narrated by al-Tabari, al-Nisaburi, and mentioned by al-Baydawi and Ibn al-Jawzi, to clarify to him that – assuming it is sound – it is not suitable as a basis for casting any defect on the Messenger of Allah, and a large group of hadith scholars and Quran commentators have declared it weak, including al-Qurtubi and Ibn Kathir. They said: The sound and reliable narration in this regard is what was narrated from Ali ibn al-Husayn that the Prophet had been inspired = it is the doubt or problem: that Allah wanted to marry His Messenger to the divorced wife of his adopted son for a specific legislative wisdom, so He prepared for that its well-known human means?! Rather, let me say to you: what is wrong with the heart of the Messenger of Allah being moved with inclination towards her? And when was the inclination of hearts an action subject to a ruling of the Shari'ah? Indeed, the whole world knows that heart's inclination is not among voluntary and choice-based actions. Moreover, I mention the involuntary emotions, and not [؟] that the Messenger of Allah had seen her before he married her to Zayd, and if the matter were one of desire, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her himself without placing between him and this marriage a formidable obstacle from Jahili customs. When Zayd divorced her after his patience was exhausted in bearing what he received from her, the revelation came down to the Messenger of Allah with this verse, peace be upon him: Allah revealed to him that Zayd will divorce Zaynab and that he will marry her by Allah's marriage of her to him. When Zayd complained to the Prophet about Zaynab's character and that she did not obey him, and informed him that he wanted to divorce her, he said to him, by way of etiquette and counsel: 'Fear Allah in your speech and keep your wife,' while he knew that he would separate from her and marry her. This is what he concealed in himself and for which the Exalted and Glorious Creator reproached him, by His saying: 'And you concealed in yourself what Allah would bring to light.' And we, we have chosen not to turn the page on the other narration that al-Tabari and others transmitted, as some see, but rather we wanted to reveal the infallibility of our master the Messenger of Allah from what a group of orientalists and people of intellectual invasion try to cast at him. Even assuming its authenticity, it does nothing, in any case, but increase him in moral excellence and sublimity of character. And there is no justification for demonstrating the Prophet's infallibility by ignoring this narration or definitively rejecting it, for by doing so you make the questioner feel that al-Tabari and those who followed his path, who did not weaken this narration, did not care to attach a defect to his character, peace be upon him. Far be it from them. Rather, this approach increases the doubts of those with scruples and weak of faith. Those who never lack a means – they come across this narration in sources that may not weaken it nor speak of its falsehood. So one of them goes on to attach a defect to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, claiming that he is following the school of al-Tabari and his likes...!!! Or claiming – maliciously – that he is attaching a defect to the Messenger of Allah on a weak probability...!! And among the most dangerous afflictions of this ignoring is that it uproots trust in the da'iyya from the souls of these people. It makes them imagine that the affair of this religion is in the hands of 'its shaykhs': if they like something, they support the hadiths about it, and if they dislike it, they close the door of discussion by declaring weakness, denial, or claiming fabrication.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Prophet's character and a discussion of how to handle narrations that might appear problematic. The author recounts the story of Zayd and Zaynab: Zayd complained about his wife, the Prophet advised him to keep her, but at one point the Prophet saw her and his heart inclined, which he dismissed. The author then addresses a doubt: whether it is problematic for the Prophet to have such an inclination. He argues that heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to legal rulings, so there is no issue. Moreover, the Prophet had seen her before and could have married her if he desired, but he did not, proving the matter was not about lust. When Zayd finally divorced her, revelation came commanding the marriage. The author then defends the authenticity of narrations that mention the Prophet's inclination, acknowledging that some scholars consider them weak, but argues that even if authentic, they do not detract from the Prophet's moral excellence. He criticizes those who ignore such narrations outright, as it may lead the questioner to doubt the honesty of scholars like al-Tabari, and it may allow those with weak faith to exploit the narrations to attack the Prophet. The author concludes by warning that such ignoring uproots trust in Islamic da'wa, as it makes people think scholars manipulate hadiths based on personal preference.

Key Terms
ميل القلبي
مقلب القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say when his heart moved towards Zaynab?
A) Keep your wife and fear Allah
B) Glory be to Allah, the Turner of Hearts
C) I desire her
D) This is unlawful

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's immediate turning to Allah upon feeling an inclination shows his profound taqwa and reliance on Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a strong pull towards something you know is not right for you—whether a relationship, a habit, or a desire—do you immediately turn to Allah like the Prophet did, or do you dwell on it? What one concrete action can you take today to imitate his response?
?
The Prophet said, 'Glory be to Allah, the Turner of Hearts.' Do you truly believe that Allah alone controls your heart and its attachments? If so, why do you still hold on to feelings or people that lead you away from Him? What would change if you sincerely asked Allah to turn your heart towards what pleases Him?
?
Zayd was repeatedly told to keep his wife and fear Allah, despite his complaints. Are there relationships or situations in your life where you focus on faults rather than exercising patience and taqwa? How can you apply the Prophet's advice to your own circumstances this week?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Prophet's Heart Inclination is Involuntary
Buti argues that heart inclinations are involuntary and thus do not affect the Prophet's infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's momentary heart inclination does not contradict his infallibility, because such emotions are involuntary and not subject to moral judgment.

Core Idea
Heart inclinations are involuntary; they do not affect the Prophet's moral excellence.

Buti addresses a key doubt: how can the Prophet, who is infallible, experience an emotional inclination towards a woman who is not his wife? He argues that heart movements are not under voluntary control and thus are not subject to divine commands. This lesson examines his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt
Read the question Buti poses: 'What is wrong with the heart of the Messenger of Allah being moved with inclination towards her?'
This is the central doubt he refutes.
2
Understand his argument
Notice that he asks: 'When was the inclination of hearts an action subject to a ruling of the Shari'ah?' He distinguishes between voluntary actions and involuntary emotions.
The key distinction is between 'actions' and 'involuntary emotions'.
3
Reinforce with evidence
Buti adds that the Prophet had seen Zaynab earlier and could have married her if he desired, but he did not. This proves the later inclination was not due to lust.
This is a secondary argument showing his prior restraint.

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Prophet's character and a discussion of how to handle narrations that might appear problematic. The author recounts the story of Zayd and Zaynab: Zayd complained about his wife, the Prophet advised him to keep her, but at one point the Prophet saw her and his heart inclined, which he dismissed. The author then addresses a doubt: whether it is problematic for the Prophet to have such an inclination. He argues that heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to legal rulings, so there is no issue. Moreover, the Prophet had seen her before and could have married her if he desired, but he did not, proving the matter was not about lust. When Zayd finally divorced her, revelation came commanding the marriage. The author then defends the authenticity of narrations that mention the Prophet's inclination, acknowledging that some scholars consider them weak, but argues that even if authentic, they do not detract from the Prophet's moral excellence. He criticizes those who ignore such narrations outright, as it may lead the questioner to doubt the honesty of scholars like al-Tabari, and it may allow those with weak faith to exploit the narrations to attack the Prophet. The author concludes by warning that such ignoring uproots trust in Islamic da'wa, as it makes people think scholars manipulate hadiths based on personal preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's heart inclination towards Zaynab was a moral failing or a sign of lust.
Correction: Heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to moral judgment; the Prophet's prior restraint shows his character.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why is the Prophet's heart inclination not a sin?
A) Because it was a command from Allah
B) Because heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to Shari'ah rulings
C) Because the narration is weak
D) Because Zaynab was not yet married

Key Takeaway
Involuntary emotions do not detract from the Prophet's sinlessness; only voluntary actions are subject to divine command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mistakenly held a grudge against someone for a facial expression they couldn't control? How does this lesson reframe your understanding of what is truly blameworthy?
?
When you feel an involuntary dislike for someone, do you immediately assume it's a moral failing? How can you use the Prophet's example to separate involuntary feelings from voluntary actions?
?
This lesson argues that even the Prophet experienced natural inclinations without sin. Are you willing to extend the same grace to yourself and others for involuntary emotions? What would change in your life if you did?

Confronting Problematic Narrations
Buti criticizes the strategy of ignoring problematic narrations and warns of its negative consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn Buti's method of dealing with narrations that appear problematic: not ignoring them, but explaining them in a way that upholds the Prophet's excellence.

Core Idea
Ignoring problematic narrations can backfire; instead, engage and explain them properly.

Buti criticizes the approach of simply ignoring or rejecting narrations that seem to cast doubt on the Prophet. He argues that this can lead to greater skepticism and damage trust in scholars. This lesson presents his alternative: face the narration, show that even if authentic it does not harm the Prophet's status, and thereby strengthen faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique
Buti says some choose to ignore the narration, but that can make people doubt the integrity of scholars like al-Tabari.
He is concerned about the psychological impact on the questioner.
2
Identify the dangers
List the three dangers Buti mentions: (1) people with weak faith exploit it, (2) they accuse scholars of hiding defects, (3) trust in da'wa is uprooted.
3
Understand the alternative
Buti advocates exposing the narration and showing its compatibility with the Prophet's infallibility.
This is a proactive defense.

وهذا ماحدث : فقد تعكر صفو العيش بينهما . وكان زيد يشكو منها غلظة القول وعصيان الأمر والأذى باللسان والتعظم بالشرف ، وأقبل مراراً يستأذن رسول الله في طلاقها ، فيقول له عليه الصلاة والسلام في كل مرة : أمسك عليك زوجك واتق الله . وربما أبصرها خلال هذه المدة ، ذات يوم ، فتحرك قلبه نحوها ، فأشاح بوجهه قائلاً بينه وبين نفسه : « سبحان الله مقلب القلوب فقد ذكرت روايات شيئاً من هذا القبيل، ولست أدري ماهو هذا الذي يدعو إلى التحرج من قبول هذه الرواية أو استشكالها أو الوقوف عندها ) . ماذا من (۱) نقول هذا الكلام لمن رأى أن يتمسك بهذه الرواية التي أشرنا إليها ، ويعدها رواية صحيحة ، اتباعاً لما رواه الطبري والنيسابوري وذكره البيضاوي وابن الجوزي لنوضح له أنها - على فرض أنها صحيحة - لا تصلح معتمداً لبث أي نقيصة في جانب رسول الله وقد ضعفها جمع كبير من علماء الحديث وأئمة التفسير ، ومنهم القرطبي وابن كثير ، قالوا : والرواية الصحيحة المعتمدة في ذلك ما روي عن علي بن الحسين أن النبي كان قد أوحى = هي الشبهة أو الإشكال في أن يريد الله أن يزوج رسوله من مطلقة متبناه لحكمة تشريعية معينة ، فيهيء لذلك سبيله الإنساني المعروف ؟! بل دعني أقول لـك ماذا في أن يتحرك قلب رسول الله الله بالميل إليها ؟ ومتى كان ميل القلوب فعلاً يتعلق به حكم من أحكام الشريعة وقد علمت الدنيـا بـأسـرهـا أن الميل القلبي الأفعال الكسبية والاختيارية ؟ على أني أذكر الانفعالات القسرية وليس من من مرة أخرى أن رسول الله لا و كان قد رآها قبل أن يزوجها من زيد ، ولو أن المسألة كانت مسألة طمع فيها لما منعه أي مانع من أن يتزوج هو منها دون أن بضع بينه وبين هذا الزواج عقبة كأداء من الأعراف الجاهلية . فلما طلقها زيد بعد أن نفذ صبره على احتمال ماكان يلقى منها ، نزل الوحي على رسول الله بهذه الآية صلى الله عليه وسلم : الله إليه أن زيداً يطلق زينب وأنه يتزوجها بتزويج الله إياها . فلما تشكى زيد للنبي خلق زينب وأنها لا تطيعه وأعلمه أنه يريد طلاقها ، قال له على جهة الأدب والوصية : « اتق الله في قولك وأمسك عليك زوجك » وهو يعلم أنه سيفارقها ويتزوجها ، فهذا هو الذي أخفاه في نفسه وعاتبه عليه الباري جل جلاله ، بقوله وتخفي في نفسك ما الله مبديه . ونحن ، فقد آثرنا أن لا نضرب صفحاً عن الرواية الأخرى التي ساقها الطبري وآخرون ، كما يرى البعض ، بل أحببنا أن نكشف عن عصمة سيدنا رسول الله عما يرميـه بـه طائفة من المستشرقين وأرباب الغزو الفكري ، حتى على فرض صحتها ، فهي لا تزيده - على كل حال - إلا رفعة في الخلق وسموا في الجانب . ولا مسوغ لبيان عصمة النبي على أساس تجاهل هذه الرواية أو القطع ببطلانها ، فأنت بذلك تشعر السائل أن الطبري ومن جرى مجراه ممن لم يضعف هذه الرواية لم يبالوا أن يلحقوا النقيصة بخلقه عليه الصلاة والسلام . وحاشاهم عن ذلك . بل إن شأنه أن يزيد في شكوك أصحاب الوساوس وضعاف الإيمان . أولئك الذين لا يعدمون وسيلة من يطلعون منها على هذه الرواية في مصادر قد لا تضعفها ولا تتحدث عن بطلانها . فيمضي أحدهم يلحق النقيصة برسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام زاعماً أنه يسير في ذلك على مذهب الطبري وأمثاله ..!!! أو زاعماً - بخبث - أنه يلحق النقيصة برسول الله على احتمال ضعيف ..!! ومن أخطر آفات هذا التجاهل أنه يقتلع الثقة بالداعية من نفوس هؤلاء الناس ، إنه يجعلهم يتصورون أن أمر هذا الدين بيد « مشايخه » فإذا أعجبهم شيء منه دعموا الأحاديث الواردة فيه وإذا لم يعجبهم أغلقوا طريق النقاش فيه بالتضعيف أو الإنكار أو ادعاء الوضع ( - ۲۱۱ -
And this is what happened: the tranquility of life between them was disturbed. Zayd complained to him of her harsh speech, disobedience of command, verbal harm, and boasting of lineage, and he repeatedly asked the Messenger of Allah for permission to divorce her. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said to him each time: 'Keep your wife and fear Allah.' And perhaps he saw her during this period, one day, and his heart moved towards her, so he turned his face away, saying to himself: 'Glory be to Allah, the Turner of Hearts...' Narrations have mentioned something of this sort, and I do not know what it is that calls for reluctance to accept this narration or to find it problematic or to pause at it. What is (1) we say this to one who sees fit to cling to this narration we have indicated, and considers it a sound narration, following what was narrated by al-Tabari, al-Nisaburi, and mentioned by al-Baydawi and Ibn al-Jawzi, to clarify to him that – assuming it is sound – it is not suitable as a basis for casting any defect on the Messenger of Allah, and a large group of hadith scholars and Quran commentators have declared it weak, including al-Qurtubi and Ibn Kathir. They said: The sound and reliable narration in this regard is what was narrated from Ali ibn al-Husayn that the Prophet had been inspired = it is the doubt or problem: that Allah wanted to marry His Messenger to the divorced wife of his adopted son for a specific legislative wisdom, so He prepared for that its well-known human means?! Rather, let me say to you: what is wrong with the heart of the Messenger of Allah being moved with inclination towards her? And when was the inclination of hearts an action subject to a ruling of the Shari'ah? Indeed, the whole world knows that heart's inclination is not among voluntary and choice-based actions. Moreover, I mention the involuntary emotions, and not [؟] that the Messenger of Allah had seen her before he married her to Zayd, and if the matter were one of desire, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her himself without placing between him and this marriage a formidable obstacle from Jahili customs. When Zayd divorced her after his patience was exhausted in bearing what he received from her, the revelation came down to the Messenger of Allah with this verse, peace be upon him: Allah revealed to him that Zayd will divorce Zaynab and that he will marry her by Allah's marriage of her to him. When Zayd complained to the Prophet about Zaynab's character and that she did not obey him, and informed him that he wanted to divorce her, he said to him, by way of etiquette and counsel: 'Fear Allah in your speech and keep your wife,' while he knew that he would separate from her and marry her. This is what he concealed in himself and for which the Exalted and Glorious Creator reproached him, by His saying: 'And you concealed in yourself what Allah would bring to light.' And we, we have chosen not to turn the page on the other narration that al-Tabari and others transmitted, as some see, but rather we wanted to reveal the infallibility of our master the Messenger of Allah from what a group of orientalists and people of intellectual invasion try to cast at him. Even assuming its authenticity, it does nothing, in any case, but increase him in moral excellence and sublimity of character. And there is no justification for demonstrating the Prophet's infallibility by ignoring this narration or definitively rejecting it, for by doing so you make the questioner feel that al-Tabari and those who followed his path, who did not weaken this narration, did not care to attach a defect to his character, peace be upon him. Far be it from them. Rather, this approach increases the doubts of those with scruples and weak of faith. Those who never lack a means – they come across this narration in sources that may not weaken it nor speak of its falsehood. So one of them goes on to attach a defect to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, claiming that he is following the school of al-Tabari and his likes...!!! Or claiming – maliciously – that he is attaching a defect to the Messenger of Allah on a weak probability...!! And among the most dangerous afflictions of this ignoring is that it uproots trust in the da'iyya from the souls of these people. It makes them imagine that the affair of this religion is in the hands of 'its shaykhs': if they like something, they support the hadiths about it, and if they dislike it, they close the door of discussion by declaring weakness, denial, or claiming fabrication.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Prophet's character and a discussion of how to handle narrations that might appear problematic. The author recounts the story of Zayd and Zaynab: Zayd complained about his wife, the Prophet advised him to keep her, but at one point the Prophet saw her and his heart inclined, which he dismissed. The author then addresses a doubt: whether it is problematic for the Prophet to have such an inclination. He argues that heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to legal rulings, so there is no issue. Moreover, the Prophet had seen her before and could have married her if he desired, but he did not, proving the matter was not about lust. When Zayd finally divorced her, revelation came commanding the marriage. The author then defends the authenticity of narrations that mention the Prophet's inclination, acknowledging that some scholars consider them weak, but argues that even if authentic, they do not detract from the Prophet's moral excellence. He criticizes those who ignore such narrations outright, as it may lead the questioner to doubt the honesty of scholars like al-Tabari, and it may allow those with weak faith to exploit the narrations to attack the Prophet. The author concludes by warning that such ignoring uproots trust in Islamic da'wa, as it makes people think scholars manipulate hadiths based on personal preference.

Key Terms
رواية
عصمة
تضعيف
إنكار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The best way to defend the Prophet is to reject any problematic narration outright.
Correction: Buti says ignoring can backfire; instead, engage with the narration and explain it within the framework of infallibility.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say is the most dangerous affliction of ignoring the narration?
A) It angers the scholars
B) It uproots trust in the da'iyya
C) It causes the narration to be forgotten
D) It contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
A robust defense of the Prophet requires confronting, not ignoring, narrations that seem problematic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a hadith that seems to contradict what you believe about the Prophet, is your first instinct to dismiss it or to investigate it? What does your reaction say about your trust in the Prophet's character?
?
Buti says ignoring problematic narrations uproots people's trust in you as a da'iyya. Think of a time you avoided a tough question about Islam. Did that strengthen or weaken the questioner's trust? How might you respond differently now?
?
Are you willing to face the possibility that some narrations might be authentic and still believe that they only enhance the Prophet's excellence? Or do you feel safer hiding them? What does your answer reveal about your own certainty in the Prophet's perfection?

Prophethood
beginner

Heart Inclinations Are Not Voluntary Acts
Buti argues that heart inclination is not a voluntary act subject to sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's possible heart inclination towards Zaynab does not imply any wrongdoing, as heart inclinations are not voluntary acts subject to sharia rulings.

Core Idea
Heart inclinations are not voluntary actions; they carry no legal judgment.

The suspicion that the Prophet married Zaynab out of personal desire rests on the assumption that his heart's inclination would be blameworthy. Buti immediately dismantles this by clarifying the nature of heart feelings. Even if such an inclination existed, it would not be a matter of sharia ruling because it is not a voluntary act. He further points out that the Prophet could have married her earlier if he had desired her, but he did not, proving his intention was not personal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand Buti's argument.
2
Identify Buti's two arguments
Notice how Buti first argues that heart inclinations are not subject to sharia, then adds that the Prophet could have married Zaynab earlier if he had desired her.
These two points together refute the suspicion.
3
Reflect on the category of acts
Think about the distinction between voluntary acts (which have ruling) and involuntary emotions (which do not). Why does this distinction matter for the Prophet's infallibility?
This connects to the broader principle of 'isma.

Source Text

أو زاعماً - بخبث - أنه يلحق النقيصة برسول الله على احتمال ضعيف ..!! ومن أخطر آفات هذا التجاهل أنه يقتلع الثقة بالداعية من نفوس هؤلاء الناس ، إنه يجعلهم يتصورون أن أمر هذا الدين بيد « مشايخه » فإذا أعجبهم شيء منه دعموا الأحاديث الواردة فيه وإذا لم يعجبهم أغلقوا طريق النقاش فيه بالتضعيف أو الإنكار أو ادعاء الوضع
The suspicion or objection is that Allah wanted to marry His Messenger to the divorced wife of his adopted son for a specific legislative wisdom, so He prepared for that its known human means?! Rather, let me say to you: what is wrong with the heart of the Messenger of Allah moving with inclination towards her? And when was the inclination of hearts ever an act subject to a ruling from the rulings of sharia, when the whole world knows that heart inclination is not among voluntary and optional acts? Moreover, I mention non-voluntary emotions, and not once... that the Messenger of Allah had seen her before he married her to Zayd, and if the matter were a matter of greed for her, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her himself without there being an obstacle between him and this marriage as difficult as the pre-Islamic customs. Then when Zayd divorced her after his patience ran out in enduring what he used to receive from her, revelation came down to the Messenger of Allah with this verse: Allah informed him that Zayd would divorce Zaynab and that he would marry her by Allah's marriage of her to him. Far be it from them! Rather, it would increase the doubts of those with whisperings and the weak of faith. Those who do not lack a means by which they come across this narration in sources that may not weaken it nor speak of its falsehood. Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting the objection: some claim that Allah arranged for the Prophet to marry Zaynab, the divorced wife of his adopted son Zayd, simply to satisfy a personal desire, using ordinary human means. The author immediately refutes this by questioning the premise: even if the Prophet's heart inclined toward her, heart inclinations are not voluntary actions subject to sharia rulings; they are non-voluntary emotions. Moreover, the Prophet had seen Zaynab before her marriage to Zayd, and if he had coveted her, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her then, despite pre-Islamic customs. Then the author recounts the actual divine command: Zayd divorced Zaynab after his patience ended, and revelation informed the Prophet that he would marry her. When Zayd complained, the Prophet told him to keep his wife, knowing he would eventually divorce her and the Prophet would marry her—this is what he hid in his heart, for which Allah reproached him in verse 33:37. The author then discusses a narration from al-Tabari that some use to criticize the Prophet, but he argues that even if authentic, it only shows the Prophet's high character. He warns against ignoring such narrations, as doing so undermines trust in scholars and allows doubters to exploit them. The author concludes by stressing that suppressing discussion weakens faith and confidence in religious leadership.

ميل قلبي
شريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any inclination of the heart towards a woman is sinful for a prophet.
Correction: Heart inclinations are involuntary emotions not subject to sharia rulings; they do not affect the Prophet's infallibility.

Checkpoint
What is Buti's main argument against the suspicion that the Prophet married Zaynab out of personal desire in this passage?
A) The Prophet never saw Zaynab before her marriage to Zayd.
B) Heart inclinations are not voluntary actions subject to sharia.
C) The marriage was forced by the companions.
D) Zaynab was not attractive.

Key Takeaway
Heart inclinations are involuntary and not subject to sharia rulings, so a prophet's inclination does not imply sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you felt an involuntary heart inclination that you were tempted to treat as sinful? How does this lesson change the way you view such feelings?
?
If heart inclinations are not subject to sharia, then where does moral responsibility begin for you? Are you ready to stop judging others for feelings they cannot control, and instead focus on your own voluntary choices?
?
The Prophet's heart inclination was not a sin. But what about your own heart? What secret inclinations are you harboring that you have not yet brought under the authority of your voluntary actions? Will you examine them today?

The Divine Command and the Prophet's Hidden Knowledge
Buti recounts the divine command behind the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the revelation commanded the Prophet to marry Zaynab, and why the Prophet's hidden knowledge of this command does not contradict his infallibility.

Core Idea
The Prophet married Zaynab by divine command, not personal desire.

The suspicion of personal desire is further refuted by the fact that the marriage was commanded by revelation. Buti narrates the sequence: Zayd divorced Zaynab after his patience ended, and Allah revealed to the Prophet that he would marry her. When Zayd complained, the Prophet advised him to keep his wife, knowing that the divorce was inevitable. This hidden knowledge is referred to in the Quran, and Buti explains it as part of the divine plan, not a flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the revelation
Read the Arabic text describing Zayd's divorce and the revelation. Note how the Prophet's actions are guided by divine command.
2
Understand the Prophet's hidden knowledge
Identify what the Prophet hid in himself: that Allah would command him to marry Zaynab after Zayd divorced her. This is mentioned in the Quranic reproach.
The reproach is not for wrongdoing but for not being fully transparent about the command.
3
Connect to infallibility
Reflect on how this narrative shows the Prophet's obedience to Allah, not personal whim. His counsel to Zayd was based on patience, not deception.
This reinforces 'isma.

الشبهة أو الإشكال في أن يريد الله أن يزوج رسوله من مطلقة متبناه لحكمة تشريعية معينة ، فيهيء لذلك سبيله الإنساني المعروف ؟! بل دعني أقول لـك ماذا في أن يتحرك قلب رسول الله الله بالميل إليها ؟ ومتى كان ميل القلوب فعلاً يتعلق به حكم من أحكام الشريعة وقد علمت الدنيـا بـأسـرهـا أن الميل القلبي الأفعال الكسبية والاختيارية ؟ على أني أذكر الانفعالات القسرية وليس من من مرة أخرى أن رسول الله لا و كان قد رآها قبل أن يزوجها من زيد ، ولو أن المسألة كانت مسألة طمع فيها لما منعه أي مانع من أن يتزوج هو منها دون أن بضع بينه وبين هذا الزواج عقبة كأداء من الأعراف الجاهلية . فلما طلقها زيد بعد أن نفذ صبره على احتمال ماكان يلقى منها ، نزل الوحي على رسول الله بهذه الآية صلى الله عليه وسلم : الله إليه أن زيداً يطلق زينب وأنه يتزوجها بتزويج الله إياها . فلما تشكى زيد للنبي خلق زينب وأنها لا تطيعه وأعلمه أنه يريد طلاقها ، قال له على جهة الأدب والوصية : « اتق الله في قولك وأمسك عليك زوجك » وهو يعلم أنه سيفارقها ويتزوجها ، فهذا هو الذي أخفاه في نفسه وعاتبه عليه الباري جل جلاله ، بقوله وتخفي في نفسك ما الله مبديه . ونحن ، فقد آثرنا أن لا نضرب صفحاً عن الرواية الأخرى التي ساقها الطبري وآخرون ، كما يرى البعض ، بل أحببنا أن نكشف عن عصمة سيدنا رسول الله عما يرميـه بـه طائفة من المستشرقين وأرباب الغزو الفكري ، حتى على فرض صحتها ، فهي لا تزيده - على كل حال - إلا رفعة في الخلق وسموا في الجانب . ولا مسوغ لبيان عصمة النبي على أساس تجاهل هذه الرواية أو القطع ببطلانها ، فأنت بذلك تشعر السائل أن الطبري ومن جرى مجراه ممن لم يضعف هذه الرواية لم يبالوا أن يلحقوا النقيصة بخلقه عليه الصلاة والسلام . وحاشاهم عن ذلك . بل إن شأنه أن يزيد في شكوك أصحاب الوساوس وضعاف الإيمان . أولئك الذين لا يعدمون وسيلة من يطلعون منها على هذه الرواية في مصادر قد لا تضعفها ولا تتحدث عن بطلانها . فيمضي أحدهم يلحق النقيصة برسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام زاعماً أنه يسير في ذلك على مذهب الطبري وأمثاله ..!!! أو زاعماً - بخبث - أنه يلحق النقيصة برسول الله على احتمال ضعيف ..!! ومن أخطر آفات هذا التجاهل أنه يقتلع الثقة بالداعية من نفوس هؤلاء الناس ، إنه يجعلهم يتصورون أن أمر هذا الدين بيد « مشايخه » فإذا أعجبهم شيء منه دعموا الأحاديث الواردة فيه وإذا لم يعجبهم أغلقوا طريق النقاش فيه بالتضعيف أو الإنكار أو ادعاء الوضع
The suspicion or objection is that Allah wanted to marry His Messenger to the divorced wife of his adopted son for a specific legislative wisdom, so He prepared for that its known human means?! Rather, let me say to you: what is wrong with the heart of the Messenger of Allah moving with inclination towards her? And when was the inclination of hearts ever an act subject to a ruling from the rulings of sharia, when the whole world knows that heart inclination is not among voluntary and optional acts? Moreover, I mention non-voluntary emotions, and not once... that the Messenger of Allah had seen her before he married her to Zayd, and if the matter were a matter of greed for her, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her himself without there being an obstacle between him and this marriage as difficult as the pre-Islamic customs. Then when Zayd divorced her after his patience ran out in enduring what he used to receive from her, revelation came down to the Messenger of Allah with this verse: Allah informed him that Zayd would divorce Zaynab and that he would marry her by Allah's marriage of her to him. So when Zayd complained to the Prophet about Zaynab's character and that she did not obey him, and informed him that he wanted to divorce her, he said to him in the manner of good manners and counsel: 'Fear Allah in your speech and keep your wife to yourself,' while he knew that he would separate from her and marry her. This is what he hid in himself and for which the Exalted Lord reproached him, by His saying: 'And you hide in yourself what Allah will reveal.' And we have chosen not to turn away from the other narration brought by al-Tabari and others, as some see, but rather we wanted to reveal the infallibility of our master the Messenger of Allah from what a group of Orientalists and people of intellectual invasion accuse him of, even if it is assumed to be authentic, it does not increase him - in any case - except elevation in character and loftiness in aspect. And there is no justification for demonstrating the Prophet's infallibility on the basis of ignoring this narration or definitively declaring it false, for by doing so you make the questioner feel that al-Tabari and those like him who did not weaken this narration did not care to attach deficiency to his character, peace and blessings be upon him. Far be it from them! Rather, it would increase the doubts of those with whisperings and the weak of faith. Those who do not lack a means by which they come across this narration in sources that may not weaken it nor speak of its falsehood. So one of them goes on to attach deficiency to the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, claiming that he follows the school of al-Tabari and his likes...!!! Or claiming - maliciously - that he attaches deficiency to the Messenger of Allah on a weak probability...!! One of the most dangerous afflictions of this neglect is that it uproots confidence in the caller from the souls of these people; it makes them imagine that the matter of this religion is in the hands of 'its shaykhs'; if they like something from it, they support the hadiths reported about it, and if they do not like it, they close the door to discussion about it by weakening, denying, or claiming fabrication.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting the objection: some claim that Allah arranged for the Prophet to marry Zaynab, the divorced wife of his adopted son Zayd, simply to satisfy a personal desire, using ordinary human means. The author immediately refutes this by questioning the premise: even if the Prophet's heart inclined toward her, heart inclinations are not voluntary actions subject to sharia rulings; they are non-voluntary emotions. Moreover, the Prophet had seen Zaynab before her marriage to Zayd, and if he had coveted her, nothing would have prevented him from marrying her then, despite pre-Islamic customs. Then the author recounts the actual divine command: Zayd divorced Zaynab after his patience ended, and revelation informed the Prophet that he would marry her. When Zayd complained, the Prophet told him to keep his wife, knowing he would eventually divorce her and the Prophet would marry her—this is what he hid in his heart, for which Allah reproached him in verse 33:37. The author then discusses a narration from al-Tabari that some use to criticize the Prophet, but he argues that even if authentic, it only shows the Prophet's high character. He warns against ignoring such narrations, as doing so undermines trust in scholars and allows doubters to exploit them. The author concludes by stressing that suppressing discussion weakens faith and confidence in religious leadership.

Key Terms
الوحي
عصمة
متبنى
إخفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet deceived Zayd by advising him to keep his wife while knowing he would divorce her.
Correction: The Prophet's advice was based on good manners and patience; the hidden knowledge was about a future divine command, not deceit.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet know that he hid in himself according to the passage?
A) That Zayd would divorce Zaynab and he would marry her.
B) That Zaynab was actually a disbeliever.
C) That the marriage was forbidden.
D) That Zayd would convert to Islam.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was by direct divine command, not personal desire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you claim to trust Allah's plan, do you ever hide your true feelings or knowledge to maintain appearances? The Prophet hid nothing but a future command—what are you hiding that you know Allah will reveal?
?
The Prophet's reproach came from his human hesitation. Where in your life do you let politeness or fear of conflict override honesty about what Allah has decreed? What step will you take today to align your speech with your inner conviction?
?
If you were in the Prophet's place, would you have been able to conceal your knowledge for the sake of divine timing? Examine a situation where you rushed to reveal something when Allah wanted you to wait. How can you cultivate patience in acting on divine commands?

Handling Problematic Narrations: The Tabari Account
Buti argues for addressing problematic narrations rather than ignoring them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's approach to narrations that seem to criticize the Prophet, and why ignoring them can harm faith.

Core Idea
Ignoring weak narrations does not protect the Prophet's image; addressing them with confidence in his infallibility does.

Some scholars prefer to ignore narrations from al-Tabari that imply a flaw in the Prophet's character. Buti argues for a different approach: even if such narrations were authentic, they do not detract from the Prophet's nobility, but rather highlight his perfect character. He warns that brushing them aside can actually increase doubt, as critics will accuse scholars of covering up. The proper response is to engage with the narration and show how it is consistent with the Prophet's infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read Buti's argument about the Tabari narration
Read the Arabic passage where Buti discusses the narration from al-Tabari. Note his tone: he does not dismiss it outright.
2
Understand the two responses
Buti gives two responses: first, even if authentic, the narration only increases the Prophet's character; second, ignoring it causes more harm.
3
Reflect on the danger of ignoring
Consider Buti's warning: ignoring such narrations uproots trust in scholars and gives ammunition to critics.
This is a methodological point for defending the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Embarrassing Verse as Proof of Divine Origin
Buti uses the reproachful verse about Zainab as evidence that the Qur'an is from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's reproachful verse about the Prophet's marriage to Zainab serves as evidence that the Qur'an is from Allah and not human invention.

Core Idea
The verse the Prophet would most want to hide proves the Qur'an is from Allah.

This lesson examines a powerful argument for the divine origin of the Qur'an: the inclusion of a verse that severely reproaches the Prophet and exposes his inner feelings. If the Qur'an were from Muhammad, he would have omitted this embarrassing verse. Its preservation is evidence that it is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of verse 33:37
Read the verse carefully and note its content: it reproaches the Prophet for hiding his intention to marry Zainab and fearing people's reaction. This is a personal and potentially embarrassing revelation.
The verse is from Surah Al-Ahzab.
2
Follow Buti's rhetorical questions
The author asks two questions: what necessity would compel the Prophet to break a major Arab custom and marry his adopted son's ex-wife unless commanded by Allah? And what necessity would compel him to include this reproachful verse in the Qur'an for all ages?
These questions highlight the irrationality of the Prophet inventing such a verse.
3
Reflect on Aisha's statement and the conclusion
Aisha said that if the Prophet could hide any revelation, he would have hidden this verse. The author concludes that this incident is the greatest evidence of his prophethood and that the Qur'an is from Allah.
This ties the argument together: the very verse that seems problematic becomes proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذْ تَقُولُ الَّذِي أَنْعَمَ اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَأَنْعَمْتَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْسِكَ عَلَيْكَ زَوْجَكَ وَاتَّقِ الله ، وتُخْفِي فِي نَفْسِك ما اللهُ مُبْدِيهِ وَتَخْشَى النَّاسَ واللهُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَخْشَاهُ ، فَلَمَّا قضَى زَيْدٌ مِنْهَا وَطَراً زَوَّجُناكَهَا لِكَيْ لا يَكُونَ على المُؤْمِنِينَ حَرَجٌ فِي أَزْواج أدعيائهم إذا قضوا مِنْهُنَّ وَطَراً وَكانَ أَمْرُ الله مَفْعُولاً ) [ الأحزاب : ٣٧ ] . وَالآن لابد من أن تجيبني على هذين السؤالين : أي ضرورة هذه التي تدعو محمداً لله ) وإن سمعته لعزيزة عليه ) إلى أن علي سالم يغامر فيقتحم عادة من أهم العادات العربية ويتزوج مطلقة متبناه غير مبال بكلامهم وتقريعهم ، لولا أن حكماً إلهياً قد ساقه إلى مافعل ، بل إن الرسول ـ كما تدل الآية وكما يدل الوضع الإنساني - كان يُقدم على تنفيذ هذا الأمر الإلهي وهو مما قد يلقاه من حديث الناس عنه عندما يفاجؤون به وهو مقبل على هذا مشفق الأمر المشين جداً في أعرافهم ؟! أي ضرورة هذه التي تدعوه إلى أن يُدرج هذه الآية في القرآن فيقرأها الناس كلهم ، وهي من أول حرف فيها إلى آخر حرف عتاب للرسول شديد ، وكشف عما يخفيه في نفسه من معرفة أنه سيتزوج زينب بعد تطليق زيد لها ، أو من الميل القلبي إليها ؟ ثم هي بيان لما يخشاه من كلام قومه إذا أقدم فتزوج مطلقة متبناه . وإيضاح لحكم الله الذي لابد أن ينفذ فيه ـ نقول : أي ضرورة تدعو سيدنا محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى أن يُدرج هذه الآية في القرآن ، ويسجلها على مر الدهر كله ، لو لم يكن هذا القرآن كلام خالقه الذي لا يسعه أن يستخفي على حرف واحد منه ؟! من أجل هذا تقول عائشة فيما يرويه مسلم وغيره : ( لو كان النبي كاتماً شيئاً من الوحي لكتم هذه الآية ) وأنا ، فلعمري ما وجدت في حوادث السيرة النبوية أدل على نبوته من هذه الحادثة ، وما وجدت آية في القرآن أدل على أن القرآن كلام الله الذي
And [mention] when you said to the one upon whom Allah bestowed favor and upon whom you bestowed favor, 'Keep your wife and fear Allah,' while you hide within yourself what Allah is to disclose, and you fear the people, while Allah is more deserving that you fear Him. So when Zayd had completed his desire from her, We married her to you so that there would be no blame upon the believers concerning the wives of their adopted sons when they have completed their desire from them. And ever is the command of Allah accomplished. [Al-Ahzab: 37]. And now you must answer me these two questions: What necessity called Muhammad (peace be upon him) to risk and break one of the most important Arab customs and marry the divorced wife of his adopted son, not caring about their talk and reproach, were it not that a divine command had driven him to do what he did? Rather, the Prophet - as the verse indicates and as the human situation indicates - was proceeding to implement this divine command while he anticipated what he might encounter from people's talk when they were surprised by him approaching this matter which was very shameful in their customs? What necessity called him to include this verse in the Qur'an, so that all people recite it, while from its first letter to its last it is a severe reproach to the Prophet, and a disclosure of what he hid in himself of knowledge that he would marry Zaynab after Zayd's divorce of her, or of the heart's inclination towards her? Then it is an explanation of what he feared from his people's talk if he proceeded and married the divorced wife of his adopted son, and an clarification of Allah's command that must be implemented in him - we say: what necessity calls our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, to include this verse in the Qur'an and record it throughout all time, were it not that this Qur'an is the speech of its Creator, who cannot conceal a single letter of it? Because of this, Aisha said, as reported by Muslim and others: 'If the Prophet were to conceal anything of the revelation, he would have concealed this verse.' And I, by my life, I have not found in the events of the Prophet's biography anything more indicative of his prophethood than this incident, nor have I found a verse in the Qur'an more indicative that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah which...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage begins by quoting the Quranic verse (33:37) which recounts the incident of the Prophet's marriage to Zainab, including the reproach that he hid in himself what Allah would reveal. The author then poses two rhetorical questions to the reader. First, what necessity would compel the Prophet to break a major Arab custom by marrying his adopted son's ex-wife, exposing himself to severe criticism, unless he was acting under a divine command? Second, what necessity would compel him to include this verse—full of severe reproach and disclosure of his inner feelings—in the Qur'an for all generations to recite, if he had any choice in the matter? The author argues that this could only happen if the Qur'an is truly the speech of Allah, who cannot conceal any letter of it. The author then cites Aisha's famous statement that if the Prophet could hide any revelation, he would have hidden this verse. Finally, the author declares that this incident is the greatest evidence of his prophethood, and this verse the greatest evidence that the Qur'an is from Allah.

Key Terms
وحي
عتاب
حكمة تشريعية
نبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet could have omitted or altered parts of the Qur'an to avoid embarrassment.
Correction: This passage shows that the Prophet could not conceal any part of the revelation, even when it personally reproached him, proving the Qur'an is from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the inclusion of verse 33:37 in the Qur'an evidence that the Qur'an is from Allah?
A) Because it contains a legal ruling that benefits Muslims.
B) Because it discloses the Prophet's inner feelings and reproaches him, which he would have concealed if he had the power.
C) Because it was revealed to comfort the Prophet.
D) Because it praises the Prophet's obedience.

Key Takeaway
The inclusion of the embarrassing verse 33:37 is compelling evidence that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah and not from Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there truths in your life that you avoid speaking or acting upon because they would embarrass you or damage your reputation? How does the Prophet's example—obeying Allah despite public shame—challenge your own fears?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you ever find verses that unsettle you or confront your desires? How will you respond to those verses—by submitting to them as divine speech or by seeking to avoid them?
?
If you were in the Prophet's position, would you have included a verse that exposes your own shortcomings? What does this tell you about the level of honesty and submission required to be a true believer?

The Zaynab Incident as Proof of Divine Revelation
Buti uses the Zaynab incident to argue the Quran is divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic account of the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab serves as a powerful argument that the Quran is the speech of God, not human composition.

Core Idea
The Quran's self-rebuke in the Zaynab verse is proof it is from God, not Muhammad.

One of the most compelling arguments for the divine origin of the Quran comes from a verse that, at first glance, seems embarrassing for the Prophet Muhammad. Buti uses this very verse to show that no human author would include such self-critical material, making it a powerful sign of prophethood. In this lesson, we will follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse (33:37)
Start by reading the verse that recounts the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab. Notice the tone of rebuke and the disclosure of inner feelings.
The verse is quoted at the beginning of the passage.
2
Understand Buti's first question
Buti asks: what necessity would drive the Prophet to break a major custom unless compelled by divine command? Reflect on the social cost.
The first question challenges the idea of human authorship.
3
Understand Buti's second question
Buti asks: why would the Prophet include a verse that rebukes him and reveals his hidden intentions? No human author would do that.
This question directly points to divine origin.
4
Consider Aisha's statement
Buti quotes Aisha's famous remark that if the Prophet had concealed any revelation, he would have concealed this verse. This supports the argument.
Aisha's testimony adds weight from within the tradition.
5
Appreciate the conclusion
Buti concludes that this incident is the strongest evidence for prophethood and that the Quran is God's speech. He invites rational people to see this truth.
The argument is presented as self-evident to the rational mind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذْ تَقُولُ الَّذِي أَنْعَمَ اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَأَنْعَمْتَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْسِكَ عَلَيْكَ زَوْجَكَ وَاتَّقِ الله، وتُخْفِي فِي نَفْسِك ما اللهُ مُبْدِيهِ وَتَخْشَى النَّاسَ واللهُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَخْشَاهُ، فَلَمَّا قضَى زَيْدٌ مِنْهَا وَطَراً زَوَّجُناكَهَا لِكَيْ لا يَكُونَ على المُؤْمِنِينَ حَرَجٌ فِي أَزْواج أدعيائهم إذا قضوا مِنْهُنَّ وَطَراً وَكانَ أَمْرُ الله مَفْعُولاً) [الأحزاب: ٣٧]. والآن لابد من أن تجيبني على هذين السؤالين: أي ضرورة هذه التي تدعو محمداً لله) وإن سمعته لعزيزة عليه) إلى أن علي سالم يغامر فيقتحم عادة من أهم العادات العربية ويتزوج مطلقة متبناه غير مبال بكلامهم وتقريعهم، لولا أن حكماً إلهياً قد ساقه إلى مافعل، بل إن الرسول ـ كما تدل الآية وكما يدل الوضع الإنساني - كان يُقدم على تنفيذ هذا الأمر الإلهي وهو مما قد يلقاه من حديث الناس عنه عندما يفاجؤون به وهو مقبل على هذا مشفق الأمر المشين جداً في أعرافهم؟! أي ضرورة هذه التي تدعوه إلى أن يُدرج هذه الآية في القرآن فيقرأها الناس كلهم، وهي من أول حرف فيها إلى آخر حرف عتاب للرسول شديد، وكشف عما يخفيه في نفسه من معرفة أنه سيتزوج زينب بعد تطليق زيد لها، أو من الميل القلبي إليها؟ ثم هي بيان لما يخشاه من كلام قومه إذا أقدم فتزوج مطلقة متبناه. وإيضاح لحكم الله الذي لابد أن ينفذ فيه ـ نقول: أي ضرورة تدعو سيدنا محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى أن يُدرج هذه الآية في القرآن، ويسجلها على مر الدهر كله، لو لم يكن هذا القرآن كلام خالقه الذي لا يسعه أن يستخفي على حرف واحد منه؟! من أجل هذا تقول عائشة فيما يرويه مسلم وغيره: (لو كان النبي كاتماً شيئاً من الوحي لكتم هذه الآية). وأنا، فلعمري ما وجدت في حوادث السيرة النبوية أدل على نبوته من هذه الحادثة، وما وجدت آية في القرآن أدل على أن القرآن كلام الله الذي لا دخل لمحمد صل الله في حرف واحد منه، من الآية التي نزلت بسبب هذه الحادثة. وبوسع أي عاقل أن يبصر هذا الذي أراه ولكن لاحيلة لنا، كما قلت لك، في أن نعالج بشيء من هذه الحقائق حقد الحاقدين، أو عصبية المتعصبين، أو غيظ المغتاظين. ونشهد أن لا قبل لنا بشيء من ذلك إلا أننا نسأل الله تعالى لأنفسنا ولجميع الناس التوفيق إلى التحرر من كل سلطان إلا سلطان العقل وحده، وإلى معرفة أن قطار العمر الذي يغذ السير بنا مسرعاً إلى الموت لا يغنيه شيئاً عن الموت أو عما وراء الموت أن نحقد ونتعصب ونسوق الفكر تحت سياطهما إلى ما يشاءه سلطانها، ولكن الذي يغنيه في ذلك أن نعرف الحق الذي هو الحق، ثم نتمسك به لا لشيء إلا لأنه الحق
And when you said to the one upon whom Allah bestowed favor and you bestowed favor, 'Keep your wife and fear Allah,' and you concealed in yourself what Allah would bring to light, and you feared the people, while Allah has more right that you fear Him. So when Zayd fulfilled his need from her, We gave her to you in marriage so that there would be no difficulty for the believers concerning the wives of their adopted sons when they have fulfilled their need from them. And the command of Allah is to be carried out. [Quran 33:37]. Now you must answer me these two questions: What necessity is this that calls Muhammad (peace be upon him), even though he is sensitive to what is said about him, to take the risk of breaking one of the most important Arab customs and marry the divorced wife of his adopted son, heedless of their talk and reproach, unless a divine decree drove him to do what he did? Indeed, the Messenger—as the verse indicates and as the human situation indicates—was proceeding to execute this divine command while fearing what he might encounter from people's gossip when they are surprised by it, and he was apprehensive about this matter which was very shameful in their customs?! What necessity calls him to include this verse in the Quran for all people to read, while from its first letter to its last it is a severe rebuke to the Messenger, and a disclosure of what he hid in himself—knowledge that he would marry Zaynab after Zayd divorced her, or his inner inclination towards her? Then it is an explanation of what he feared from the talk of his people if he proceeded to marry the divorced wife of his adopted son. And a clarification of the divine command that had to be executed in him—we say: What necessity calls our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, to include this verse in the Quran and record it throughout all time, if this Quran were not the speech of its Creator, who cannot conceal a single letter of it?! For this reason, Aisha said, as narrated by Muslim and others: 'If the Prophet were to conceal any part of the revelation, he would have concealed this verse.' And I, by my life, have not found in the events of the prophetic biography anything more indicative of his prophethood than this incident, and I have not found any verse in the Quran more indicative that the Quran is the speech of Allah, in which Muhammad, peace be upon him, had no hand in a single letter, than the verse that was revealed because of this incident. And any rational person can see what I see, but we have no means, as I told you, to treat with any of these truths the hatred of the haters, or the partisanship of the bigots, or the rage of the angry. And we testify that we have no power over any of that, except that we ask Allah Almighty for ourselves and for all people success in freeing ourselves from every authority except the authority of reason alone, and in knowing that the train of life that speeds us swiftly to death—hatred, partisanship, and driving thought under their whips to whatever their authority wills—benefits it nothing against death or what lies beyond death. But what benefits it is that we know the truth that is the truth, then hold fast to it for no reason except that it is the truth.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative proof using a historical incident from the life of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) to demonstrate that the Quran is the speech of God and not the composition of the Prophet. The author begins by quoting Quran 33:37, which relates to the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh after her divorce from Zayd, the Prophet's adopted son. The verse contains a rebuke to the Prophet for hiding his intention to marry her and for fearing people's reaction. Buti then poses two rhetorical questions. First, what necessity would drive the Prophet, who was sensitive to criticism, to break a major Arab custom and marry his adopted son's divorced wife, unless a divine command compelled him? Second, what necessity would drive the Prophet to include in the Quran a verse that severely rebukes him and reveals his hidden feelings, if the Quran were his own words? He argues that no human author would expose himself in this way. To support this, he cites the famous statement of Aisha that if the Prophet were to conceal any part of revelation, he would have concealed this verse. Buti then declares that he finds no stronger evidence for prophethood than this incident, and no clearer proof that the Quran is God's speech, in which Muhammad had no part. He acknowledges that haters and bigots will not be convinced, but he invites rational people to see the truth. He concludes with a call to free oneself from all authority except reason and to hold fast to the truth for its own sake.

القرآن
النبوة
التحدي
الآية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet composed the Quran to elevate his own status and authority.
Correction: This incident shows the Prophet included a verse that rebukes him and reveals private inner feelings, which contradicts self-interest and indicates divine origin.

Checkpoint
What does Buti argue the Zaynab incident proves about the Quran?
A) The Prophet was a skilled poet.
B) The Prophet had no choice but to obey divine command, and the verse's self-rebuke shows it is from God.
C) The Prophet wanted to change Arab customs.
D) The incident is a historical error.

Key Takeaway
The Zaynab incident provides a powerful argument for the Quran's divine origin because it contains a self-rebuke that no human author would include.

?

Ruling on Belief in Miracles
Buti states the obligation of believing in miracles for all prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic ruling on belief in miracles and its basis in the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Belief in miracles is obligatory for every Muslim because they prove prophethood.

Buti clarifies that miracles are not optional additions but essential proofs of prophethood. This lesson presents the ruling and a prophetic hadith that underscores the universality of miracles. Understanding this obligation strengthens our faith in all prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the direct command 'يجب على المسلم'.
2
Identify the ruling
Find where Buti states the ruling. It begins with 'حكم الاعتقاد بها : يجب على المسلم أن يعتقد'. Understand that belief in miracles is obligatory, not optional.
The Arabic word 'يجب' indicates a legal obligation.
3
Reflect on the hadith
Read the hadith quoted by the Prophet ﷺ. Notice how it connects miracles to all prophets and emphasises the unique nature of his own miracle (the Quran).
The hadith shows that miracles are universal proofs, not exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم الاعتقاد بها : يجب على المسلم أن يعتقد بأن الله عز وجل قد جهز أنبياءه ورسله الذين أرسلهم إلى الناس بمعجزات تبين صدق دعوتهم وتوضح للناس ارتباطهم بالله جل جلاله وأنهم مؤيدون به. وما من نبي إلا وقد أكرمه الله عز وجل بمعجزة نبهت الناس إلى ضرورة الإيمان به والتمسك بهديه وفي ذلك يقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : "ما من نبي إلا وأوتي من الآيات ما مثله آمن عليه البشر ، وإنما كان الذي أوتيته وحياً أوحي إليَّ ، فأنا أرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تابعاً يوم القيامة" والآيات القرآنية التي دلت على تأييد الله أنبياءه بالمعجزات المختلفة كثيرة ومعروفة لا حاجة لنا إلى سردها
The ruling on belief in them: It is obligatory upon the Muslim to believe that Allah Almighty equipped His prophets and messengers whom He sent to people with miracles that show the truth of their call and clarify to people their connection with Allah, and that they are supported by Him. And there is no prophet except that Allah Almighty honored him with a miracle that alerted people to the necessity of believing in him and adhering to his guidance. And in that regard, the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no prophet except that he was given of signs that which would make people believe in him, and indeed what I have been given is a revelation that was revealed to me, and I hope to be the one with the most followers on the Day of Resurrection.' And the Quranic verses that indicate Allah's support of His prophets with various miracles are many and well-known, and we have no need to list them.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage states the ruling (hukm) on belief in miracles. It is obligatory for every Muslim to believe that Allah gave each prophet miracles that prove their truth and divine connection. The author then quotes a hadith where the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم says that every prophet was given signs that led people to believe, and he was given the Quran. This hadith emphasizes the universality of miracles for all prophets. The author concludes that Quranic evidence for miracles is abundant and well-known, so he does not list them.

Key Terms

أنبياء
معجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are optional beliefs that one may accept or reject.
Correction: Buti states clearly that it is obligatory upon every Muslim to believe that Allah gave prophets miracles. Rejecting them is a failure in faith.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

?

The Quran as the Prophet's Permanent Miracle
Buti explains why the Quran is the most enduring miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran is considered the greatest and most enduring miracle of Prophet Muhammad, and the wisdom behind its permanence.

Core Idea
The Quran is an eternal miracle because Muhammad's message is final until Judgment Day.

Buti turns our attention to the miracles of Prophet Muhammad, particularly the Quran. He emphasizes that believing in these miracles is obligatory and that the Quran stands out as the most eloquent and permanent sign of prophethood. This passage explains why the Quran, unlike the temporary miracles of previous prophets, remains a living testimony across all ages.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Buti's argument about the Quran as a permanent miracle.
Notice how he contrasts the Quran with other miracles.
2
Identify the key points
List the key claims: obligation to believe in miracles, the Quran as first miracle, its permanence, and the wisdom behind it.
3
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why the Quran needed to be permanent. How does this relate to the finality of prophethood?
Think about the difference between temporary and eternal messages.
4
Apply to your understanding
How does this passage strengthen your belief in the Quran as a divine miracle?
This connects belief in miracles to daily faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معجزات سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم : والذي يعنينا تفصيله هنا ، هو البحث في معجزات نبينا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام وبيان وجوب الاعتقاد بها ، وأهميتها في كشف معنى النبوة وحقيقتها في حياته عليه الصلاة والسلام . وأول معجزاته التي أيده الله عز وجل بها إنما هو معجزة القرآن : وهو أبلغ وأعظم المعجزات التي أيد الله بها رسله وأنبياءه كافة . ذلك لأنها معجزة باقية على مر الزمن . ناطقة بنبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام في كل زمان ومكان ، على حين أن سائر المعجزات الأخرى التي أيد الله بها سائر أنبيائه قد انتهت وذهبت وأصبحت تاريخاً وأخباراً تذكر . والحكمة في ثبوت هذه المعجزة لرسالة سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم دون الأنبياء والرسل السابقين أن رسالة سائر الأنبياء من قبله عليه الصلاة والسلام كانت موقوتة ببعثة من يأتي من بعده . أما رسالة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فباقية إلى يوم القيامة ، فاحتاجت إلى معجزة تشهد لها خلال هذه العصور كلها
Miracles of our Master Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم: What concerns us in detail here is the research into the miracles of our Prophet Muhammad عليه الصلاة والسلام and the clarification of the obligation of believing in them, and their importance in uncovering the meaning of prophethood and its reality in his life عليه الصلاة والسلام. And the first of his miracles with which Allah Almighty supported him is indeed the miracle of the Quran: and it is the most eloquent and greatest of the miracles with which Allah supported all His messengers and prophets. That is because it is a lasting miracle across time. It speaks of his prophethood in every time and place, whereas all the other miracles with which Allah supported His other prophets have ended and gone and become history and news that are mentioned. And the wisdom in the establishment of this miracle for the message of our Master Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم, to the exclusion of the previous prophets and messengers, is that the message of all the prophets before him عليه الصلاة والسلام was time-limited until the advent of the one who came after him. As for the message of our Prophet Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم, it is lasting until the Day of Resurrection, so it needed a miracle to testify to it throughout all these ages.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage focuses specifically on the miracles of Prophet Muhammad, especially the Quran. The author states that it is obligatory to believe in his miracles. He then identifies the Quran as his greatest and most eloquent miracle. Unlike the miracles of previous prophets, which were temporary and now only historical accounts, the Quran is permanent and still speaks of his prophethood. The author explains the wisdom behind this: previous prophets' messages were limited until the next prophet, so their miracles were temporary. But the Prophet Muhammad's message lasts until Judgment Day, so it needed a miracle that would endure through all ages. Thus, the Quran serves as an eternal testimony.

Key Terms
معجزات
سيدنا محمد
القرآن
معجزة باقية
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think physical miracles are the only proof of prophethood, or that the Quran is just one miracle among many without special status.
Correction: Buti shows the Quran is the greatest and most enduring miracle, unique in its permanence, which is required because Muhammad's message is final.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the eternal miracle of Prophet Muhammad, testifying to his prophethood forever, because his message is the final and universal guidance until the Day of Resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Farid Wajdi's Denial of Miracles in the Sira
Buti quotes Farid Wajdi's rationalistic methodology for the Sira.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Farid Wajdi's rationalistic approach to the Prophetic biography and why it contradicts traditional Islamic belief in miracles.

Core Idea
Explaining away miracles by natural causes denies the Prophet's signs.

In this lesson, we examine a concrete example of the reformist trend that sought to reinterpret Islamic sources through a rationalistic lens. Farid Wajdi published articles claiming that events in the Prophet's life should not be attributed to miracles if they can be explained by ordinary causes, even if the explanation is forced. This passage shows the rejection of supernatural elements characteristic of that movement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic quote and translation. Notice how Wajdi states his methodology explicitly.
Pay attention to the phrase 'even if with some forced effort.'
2
Understand his argument
He says he avoids excess towards miracles and prefers natural explanations. What does 'forced effort' imply about his commitment?
3
Reflect on implications
If miracles can be explained away, what does that do to the proof of prophethood? How does this contradict traditional Islamic theology?
Miracles are signs from Allah; denying them undermines the message.
4
Connect to broader context
This is part of the reformist trend that tried to harmonize Islam with modern science, often at the cost of essential beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد رأينا كيف بدأ فريد وجدي ينشر سلسلة مقالاته الجريئة التي خرج بها على الناس بعنوان (السيرة المحمدية تحت ضوء العلم والفلسفة) والتي يقول فيها ما نصه: «وقد لاحظ قراؤنا أننا نحرص فيما نكتبه في هذه السيرة على أن لا نسرف في كل ناحية إلى ناحية الإعجاز، ما دام يمكن تعليلها بالأسباب العادية حتى ولو بشيء من التكلف». (۱) انظر مجلة نور الإسلام جـ ٧ المجلد ١١ وما بعده.
For we have seen how Farid Wajdi began publishing his bold series of articles that he presented to the people under the title 'The Prophetic Biography in the Light of Science and Philosophy,' in which he says verbatim: 'Our readers have noted that we are keen, in what we write in this biography, not to go to excess from every direction to the direction of the miraculous, as long as it can be explained by ordinary causes even if with some forced effort.' (1) See the magazine 'Nur al-Islam,' vol. 7, issue 11 and after.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example of the reformist trend. The author mentions that Farid Wajdi published a series of articles titled 'The Prophetic Biography in the Light of Science and Philosophy.' He quotes Wajdi stating that his approach is to avoid attributing events to miracles whenever possible, preferring natural explanations even if forced. This shows the rejection of supernatural elements characteristic of the reformist movement.

Key Terms
السيرة المحمدية
الإعجاز
الأسباب العادية
التكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That it is acceptable to explain away miracles as long as a natural cause can be found.
Correction: This methodology denies the miraculous nature of events that are meant to be signs of prophethood, and it goes against the consensus of Muslims. Miracles are part of the proof of prophethood and cannot be reduced to natural causes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what approach does Farid Wajdi follow in his writing about the Prophet's biography?
A) He emphasizes the miraculous aspects.
B) He avoids miracles and tries to explain events by ordinary causes even if forced.
C) He combines both miracles and natural explanations equally.
D) He denies the historical accuracy of the biography.

Key Takeaway
Farid Wajdi's approach of preferring natural explanations over miracles, even forced ones, represents a rejection of the miraculous in the Sira and challenges the traditional Islamic belief in prophethood's signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read or hear about a miracle in the Prophet's life, do you ever find yourself subconsciously trying to explain it away with natural reasons? What does that tendency reveal about the state of your iman?
?
Are you willing to accept a forced natural explanation for a prophetic event simply because it feels more 'reasonable'? Where does that preference come from, and how might it alienate you from the true meaning of prophethood?
?
Wajdi's methodology allowed him to ignore the miraculous even when evidence pointed to it. In your own life, do you sometimes reject divine signs because you prefer a comfortable, worldly explanation? What will you do to change that?
